# Bug ledger — the standard

`docs/bug-ledger.jsonl` is the **single, committed, machine-countable record of
every bug (or missing primitive) surfaced in `karac`.** It exists so one
question — *"are we still finding bugs, and where?"* — becomes a number you can
watch flatten, sliced by surface (codegen/ownership/…) and by source
(kata/selfhost/dogfood/internal). Flattening of the kata + dogfood slices is a
v1 launch gate; you cannot see it without consistent capture.

Before this ledger, bug records were scattered across phase trackers (by B-ID),
test comments, commit messages, and kata READMEs (by bare commit SHA), with the
`B-YYYY-MM-DD-N` convention followed only ~1 in 4 times — so the corpus was
**not countable**. This file is the fix: prose stays in the trackers/READMEs;
they just **reference the B-ID**, and the ledger is the index.

**One tracker, not two (2026-06-14).** There used to be a second, gitignored
`bugs.md` "active triage" scratchpad holding open-bug prose. Two hand-maintained
lists drift — they did (an open bug lived in one and not the other) — so it was
**retired**. `bug-ledger.jsonl` is now the *sole* source of truth you hand-edit;
open-bug prose lives in the owning phase tracker (rule 2); and the **`## Current
state` section at the bottom of this file is generated** from the ledger (Open
bugs in full, Fixed collapsed) so you never have to read raw JSON. Never edit
that block by hand — edit the ledger and run `--inject` (see Tooling).

## The rule (lightweight, enforced)

1. **Every bug surfaced → one appended JSONL line**, keyed by a `B-YYYY-MM-DD-N`
   ID (the day it was surfaced; `N` = that day's sequence). Minting a B-ID is the
   first step of triaging any bug — the same moment it lands in a tracker.
2. **The detailed prose lives in its owning phase tracker** (or kata README);
   the ledger row carries only the countable fields + a `tracker` pointer.
3. **A kata that surfaces a bug cites its B-ID(s)** in its README (not a bare
   SHA). `selfhost`/`dogfood` bugs cite the B-ID in their spike/tracker entry.
4. `scripts/bug-lint.sh` enforces 1–3 (B-ID format + uniqueness, enum ranges,
   and the cross-repo kata↔ledger link). Run it in CI.

## Schema (one JSON object per line, fields in this order)

| field | values | notes |
|---|---|---|
| `id` | `B-YYYY-MM-DD-N` | primary key, unique |
| `date` | `YYYY-MM-DD` | surfaced date = the curve's x-axis |
| `source` | `kata:<num>` · `selfhost:<comp>` · `dogfood:<name>` · `internal` | who/what surfaced it |
| `surface` | codegen · typecheck · interp · ownership · effect · lexer · parser · runtime · resolver · cli · autopar · other | which compiler phase the defect was in |
| `class` | `unported` · `shared-logic` · `port-mistake` · `""` | port-triage taxonomy (phase-12 §); empty unless it's a self-hosting port bug |
| `severity` | high · med · low | `high` = soundness / miscompile / bootstrap-critical |
| `status` | open · fixed | |
| `fix` | commit SHA · `""` | the landing commit |
| `title` | one line, ≤110 chars | |
| `tracker` | `<file>#anchor` or `kata:<n>-README` | where the prose lives |

## Tooling

```bash
python3 scripts/bug-curve.py                 # markdown report → stdout
python3 scripts/bug-curve.py --svg docs/bug-curve.svg   # + cumulative-curve SVG
python3 scripts/bug-curve.py --inject docs/bug-ledger.md  # refresh the generated
                                                          # "Current state" block
KARA_KATAS_DIR=../kara-katas ./scripts/bug-lint.sh      # integrity gate (CI)
```

**After any ledger edit, run** `--inject docs/bug-ledger.md` (refreshes the Open/
Fixed view) **and** `--svg docs/bug-curve.svg` (refreshes the curve), then
`bug-lint.sh`. The generated block can't drift from the ledger because it's never
hand-written.

## Reading the curve honestly

The historical rows are a **best-effort backfill** (2026-05 → 2026-06-13), and
the early slope reflects **when consistent record-keeping started, not the true
bug rate** — the `B-ID` convention only began ~2026-06-07, and the late-June
spike is the self-hosting + shared-enum-drop push, not a regression. The ledger
becomes a *true* signal **going forward**, where every bug is one append at
triage time. That's the whole reason for the standard: without it you can't
distinguish "bugs flattening" from "we stopped writing them down."

## Known backfill debt (does not block the curve)

- **`class` is empty** on all rows — the port-triage taxonomy was applied
  unreliably by the initial extraction, so it was blanked. Fill per-bug from the
  owning phase-12 triage when touched.
- **34 rows lack a `fix` SHA** — the trackers recorded the fix in prose, not a
  greppable SHA. `bug-lint.sh` warns (not errors) on these; backfill from
  `git log` opportunistically.
- **Pre-convention SHA-only bugs** (e.g. some early kata gaps) may still be
  uncaptured. Add them when found; don't trust the May/early-June counts as
  complete.

| B-2026-07-03-3 | 2026-07-03 | codegen | med | PRE-EXISTING codegen miscompile (independent of Self; surfaced while fixing B-2026-07-03-2): a chained `expr.method().field` where the method returns an AGGREGATE (struct) reads the wrong value (0) under `karac build`, while the let-bound form `let b = expr.method(); b.field` is correct, and `karac run` (interp) is correct. Confirmed with a CONCRETE return type (`impl W { fn m(self) -> W { W{v:self.v+1} } }`; `a.m().v` -> 0 vs bound -> 2), so it is not `Self`-specific. A SCALAR (i64) chained return is fine (`a.inc()` where inc -> i64 works), so the bug is specific to a method-call temporary of aggregate shape consumed immediately by field access — the temporary's struct slot is not materialized/addressed before the field GEP. Repro: struct W{v:i64}; impl W{fn m(self)->W{W{v:self.v+1}}}; fn main(){let a=W{v:1}; println(a.m().v);} -> build prints 0, run prints 2. Workaround: bind the call result to a local first. | B-2026-07-03-4 | 2026-07-03 | autopar | med | Auto-par-only miscompile newly reachable after B-2026-07-03-2 enabled `-> Self` builds: a STATIC associated fn returning `-> Self`, bound to a local and then used as a method receiver, produces the wrong value (0) under the DEFAULT auto-par build, while the sequential build (KARAC_AUTO_PAR=0) and interp are correct — and `--concurrency-report` says 'no parallelization opportunities detected', so the divergence is from an auto-par-path codegen decision, NOT from forming a par group. Tightly scoped: the INSTANCE `-> Self` result feeding a method is fine under auto-par, and a CONCRETE static return (`make() -> W`) feeding a method is fine — only the static `make() -> Self` source triggers it. Repro: struct W{v:i64}; trait Dbl{fn twice(self)->Self;} impl W{fn make()->Self{W{v:7}}} impl Dbl for W{fn twice(self)->Self{W{v:self.v+self.v}}} fn main(){let c=W.make(); let d=c.twice(); println(d.v);} -> auto-par build 0, seq build 14, run 14. Likely the auto-par path re-derives the static-assoc `-> Self` call result type from the original (unrewritten, `Self`) method AST rather than the concrete target, mis-materializing the binding's slot. Guarded out of the B-2026-07-03-2 e2e regression test (twice() is called on a literal-bound receiver there). | phase-7-codegen.md |
| B-2026-07-03-5 | 2026-07-03 | typecheck | med | User-defined trait impls on PRIMITIVE integer types are unsupported end-to-end despite being an intended feature (design.md shows `impl Pod for u8`, `impl From[i32] for i64`; env_build.rs references `impl Eq for u8`; a typechecker test asserts `i64` would satisfy a bound if `impl Tr for i64` existed). For `impl Tr for <int> { fn m(self) -> ... { self + ... } }`: (1) `check_impl_block` builds the self type as `Type::Named{name:"u8"}` by hand (items.rs ~1808) instead of lowering the target, so inside the method body `self` is not recognized as numeric — `self + self` errors "arithmetic operator requires numeric type, found 'u8'" for EVERY width incl i64; (2) the method is never registered on the primitive — the call site errors "no method 'm' on type 'u8'" (and a generic bound `fn f[T: Tr](x:T)` reports "`u8` does not implement `Tr`"). Under `karac run` only `impl Tr for i64` accidentally dispatches (runtime int values are i64-typed, matching the i64-keyed impl); every narrow width (u8/u16/u32/i8/i16/i32) AND u64 fail at runtime with "method 'm' not found on type 'i64' (no interpreter dispatch arm)" because the value's runtime type is width-erased to i64 while the impl is keyed on the declared narrow width. Under `karac build` all widths fail at typecheck. Repro: trait Dbl{fn dbl(self)->Self;} impl Dbl for u8{fn dbl(self)->Self{self+self}} fn main(){let a:u8=10; println(a.dbl());}. Fix spans typecheck (lower the impl target so a primitive self is numeric + register methods for primitive impl targets) + interp dispatch (key user primitive-impl dispatch on the declared width, not the erased i64). Depends on B-2026-07-03-2's `Self`-return resolution for the `-> Self` shape. | phase-5-diagnostics.md |
| B-2026-07-03-6 | 2026-07-03 | interp | high | SILENT DATA LOSS / no-op: the interpreter's `value_compare` (src/interpreter/helpers.rs) has NO arm for `Value::Struct` or `Value::EnumVariant`, so two struct (or two enum) values fall to the `_ => value_discriminant(a).cmp(&value_discriminant(b))` fallback where BOTH map to the catch-all discriminant 8 -> always Ordering::Equal. Consequences over ordered containers / sort on struct (and enum) element/key types, ALL silent-wrong under `karac run`: `SortedSet[Struct]` and `SortedMap[Struct,_]` COLLAPSE distinct keys to one (insert 3 distinct structs -> len()==1 — data loss; n11/n13), `Vec[Struct].sort()`/`sorted()` are NO-OPs that return the input order unchanged (n7: prints 3 1 2), and `min`/`max` over a Vec[Struct] are wrong. Hash-based `Set[Struct]`/`Map[Struct,_]` are UNAFFECTED (they route through derived Hash+Eq, not value_compare — n12 dedups correctly). Exactly the class FIXED for nested Vec in B-2026-06-30-15 (whose fix worked because Vec elements carry inherent order); Struct/EnumVariant are the remaining missing arms. ARCHITECTURAL wrinkle blocking a one-line arm: `value_compare` is a free fn AND backs `OrdValue::cmp`, which BTreeMap calls deep inside insert with no interpreter/type-registry access, so it cannot see struct FIELD or enum VARIANT declaration order — a naive alphabetical-field / variant-name comparison fixes the data loss but yields a WRONG order (e.g. enum Priority{Low,Med,High} would sort alphabetically High<Low<Med, and struct{last,first} would order by first). Correct fix: embed declaration order into the Struct/EnumVariant Value (or compute an ordering key with type info at SortedSet/SortedMap insert + sort call sites, where the interpreter IS in scope) so both value_compare and OrdValue reflect derived-Ord semantics. Surfaced probing narrow-width x trait (derive(Ord) on struct{i8,u8}); NOT width-specific — reproduces with i64 fields. Repros: n7 (sort no-op), n11 (SortedSet len 1), n13 (SortedMap len 1). | phase-4-interpreter.md |

| B-2026-06-14-17 | codegen | high | wasm_browser --features wasm-threads: ANY parallel program (TaskGroup.spawn/par{}) DEADLOCKS in a real browser - the canvas/output never updates. Node (worker_threads) works, so it passed E2E and looked shipped. Root cause is in the emitted threaded glue (src/wasm_glue.rs GLUE_STATIC_BODY): wasi.thread-spawn created the pthread Web Worker FROM INSIDE the calling worker (`new Worker(new URL('#kara-thread-worker', import.meta.url))` in karaThreadWorkerMain), and the caller then immediately blocks in join()/recv() on memory.atomic.wait32. In browsers a nested dedicated worker's module script is fetched on its CREATING agent's event loop; a blocked creator never turns its loop, so the sibling's script never loads (observed in headless Chrome via CDP: 91 worker targets created with url='', none ever ran their module top-level). Every spawned task sits unclaimed, join() blocks forever, and the scheduler keeps spawning workers chasing an idle one -> hard deadlock. The glue's own comment claimed 'the classic PROXY_TO_PTHREAD model' but only proxied the PROGRAM to a primary worker, NOT thread CREATION. FIXED by completing the model (Emscripten-style): route every worker's thread-spawn to the always-live MAIN thread via a shared spawn-request ring (SPAWN_CTL SAB + requestMainThreadSpawn producer + startSpawnService main-thread drain that calls spawnKaraWorkerSync); thread-spawn still allocates+returns the tid synchronously (wasi-threads ABI) and only defers Worker construction. node keeps spawning siblings directly (nodeWorkerThreads branch) - no such constraint there. Verified end-to-end in headless Chrome: examples/fathom now renders the Mandelbrot at ~120fps across 18 cores (132859/153600 non-black px, 127 colors). Surfaced building the Fathom dogfood demo (it just showed a black screen). NOT browser-CI-testable without a headless browser harness (node path can't reproduce it). Regression: src/wasm_glue.rs unit test threaded_glue_renders_pick_constants_and_machinery asserts the spawn-proxy machinery is emitted. | 1d73edbb |

The original 'bind-without-consume' hypothesis and the control_flow_match.rs locus did NOT hold: a malloc/free-balance bisect across 0890627c (interposer at O0, runtime-derived non-foldable seed) showed the struct-wrapped `Add(BinOp)` shape leaked UNCONDITIONALLY pre-fix -- the bind-ignore variant and the fully-consuming variant leaked IDENTICALLY (delta driven by allocation volume, not by consumption), disproving the consumption-gated theory; the DIRECT-payload `Add(Expr,Expr)` shape never leaked at any commit. At HEAD (with 0890627c) all four shapes -- bind-ignore, fully-consume, reconstruct-from-fresh, direct payload -- are balanced (no per-iteration growth). The match path needed NO change; closed by regression tests (tests/memory_sanitizer.rs asan_match_byvalue_* x4) that pin no-leak across both axes (struct-wrapped + direct) and both directions (leak==0, no double-free in consuming/reconstruct/Num arms) for the authoritative Linux-CI LSan gate. macOS asan green (no UAF/double-free), AOT==interp. | 0890627c |
| B-2026-06-14-30 | codegen | med | A zero-length fixed-array binding `let a: Array[T, 0] = []` passed to a `Slice[T]` parameter hard-failed AOT codegen (`karac build`) while `karac run` was correct. `compile_array_literal([])` cannot infer the element type from the empty element list, so it returns a scalar `i64 0` sentinel and the binding's slot type is registered as `i64`, not `[0 x T]`. At the call site, `coerce_to_slice`'s Array->Slice branch keys on `slot.ty` being an `ArrayType`, so it SKIPS the empty array; the raw `i64` then reaches the call where a `{ptr, i64}` slice header is expected, tripping LLVM module verification ("Call parameter type does not match function signature!  %a1 = load i64, ptr %a ... call ... (i64 %a1, i64 0)"). The interpreter accepts the same `[] -> Slice` coercion (it does not lower to a fat pointer), so only the codegen backend surfaced it. FIXED: a new `try_emit_empty_array_let` (codegen/collections.rs), wired into the let-binding path (codegen/stmts.rs) just after the zero-init repeat-let fast path and ahead of the scalar fallback, recovers the element type from the `Array[T, N]` annotation and allocates a real `[0 x T]` slot; the empty array then coerces to a zero-length slice header `{ptr, 0}` like any other array (len 0, so the pointer is never dereferenced). Non-empty array bindings and the no-annotation empty literal are unaffected (the helper returns None and falls through). Regression-guarded: tests/codegen.rs::test_e2e_empty_array_binding_to_slice_param (empty `[]` and a non-empty `[1,2,3]` to the same `Slice[i64]` param, asserts `0\n6`). | B-2026-06-17-2 | runtime | high | Unbounded ~100 B/connection memory leak in the spawn/structured-concurrency model under a long-lived accept loop (the CANONICAL server shape: loop { tg.spawn(|| handle(conn)) }, exactly examples/ws_idle_holder/src/main.kara). Surfaced by a 1M-connection Windows IOCP soak (docs/spikes/windows-iocp-scale-investigation.md): a TaskGroup.spawn echo server's RSS climbs ~5 MB/50k conns, perfectly linear, while OS handle count stays flat — it's heap (the per-task KaracTaskHandle, + a KaracParkSlot on the coro-spawn path the blocking-handler accept loop lowers through), not an OS handle. The serial inline server (no spawn) is flat over the full 1M; both TaskGroup.spawn AND free spawn leak identically. Root cause (runtime/src/scheduler.rs): karac_runtime_taskgroup_register pushes each child handle onto KaracTaskGroupHandle.children (Mutex<Vec<*mut KaracTaskHandle>>), freed ONLY by karac_runtime_taskgroup_join_and_free at the group's scope exit — which never happens in a server's infinite accept loop, so the Vec + every child grow without bound; free spawn passes group_ptr=None so the discarded handle is orphaned (never registered, never freed — src/codegen/task_group.rs). Platform-agnostic (the scheduler code is not cfg-gated; affects Linux/macOS too — Windows just surfaced it). NOT trivially fixed: eager-freeing a completed registered child is a use-after-free if the user retained+joins its handle (join on a registered child waits+copies but does not free — group is sole freer, B-2026-06-09-1), so a safe reap must be detached-gated (codegen marks discarded spawn handles detached). Fix design in the tracker: detached:AtomicBool on KaracTaskHandle + karac_runtime_task_detach FFI; codegen marks discarded spawn/tg.spawn handles detached; taskgroup_register sweeps+frees terminal detached children (terminal = state!=PENDING non-coro, or park slot done==true coro — the slot exposes done:Mutex<bool>), bounding the Vec to live children; free spawn detached self-frees on completion. Open: the fix is memory-ownership surgery on the async hot path and must clear the Linux ASAN+LSan gate (scripts/lsan-local.sh) — the authoritative leak gate per B-2026-06-14-31/-32 — which the Windows validation box cannot run. FIXED 2026-06-17 (849030b6): detached-gated eager-reap landed. KaracTaskHandle gained detached/reaped flags + karac_runtime_task_detach FFI; codegen marks a discarded spawn/tg.spawn handle detached (pending_spawn_detach in compile_stmt -> lower_spawn_shared); karac_runtime_taskgroup_register sweeps+frees detached terminal children (UAF-safe terminal peek: notify_mutex for non-coro, new karac_runtime_park_slot_done for coro), bounding children to ~live; free-spawn non-coro worker self-reaps on completion with the detach path claiming the free exactly once under notify_mutex. Retained .join()able handles are never detached, preserving the structured wait + B-2026-06-09-1 sole-freer invariants. Verified green on the full Linux ASAN+LSan suite (263/263, scripts/lsan-local.sh): runtime unit regression taskgroup_register_reaps_detached_completed_children (asserts the children Vec stays bounded — fails pre-fix) + detached_free_spawn_self_reaps_after_completion (both reap orderings) + memory_sanitizer E2E asan_discarded_taskgroup_spawn_loop_eager_reap_no_double_free (guards the sweep<->join_and_free double-free/UAF hazard). RESIDUAL: free-spawn + coro (ws_echo_freespawn) self-reap is deferred to B-2026-06-17-3 (needs dispatcher signal-path surgery); the canonical server shape here (tg.spawn, examples/ws_idle_holder) is fully closed. | 849030b6 |
| B-2026-06-17-3 | runtime | med | Residual of B-2026-06-17-2: a discarded FREE `spawn(|| handle(conn))` whose closure tail is a coroutine-compiled blocking handler (the ws_echo_freespawn shape) still leaks its KaracTaskHandle + KaracParkSlot. The B-2026-06-17-2 fix closes the canonical `tg.spawn` server shape (group register-time sweep reaps detached terminal children, incl. coro children via park_slot_done) and free-spawn NON-coro (the pool worker self-reaps after storing terminal state). But a free-spawn CORO handle has no group to sweep it, and the ramp-worker returns the instant the coroutine suspends — completion is the dispatcher signalling the bound slot later, so the worker can't self-reap. karac_runtime_task_detach therefore only flags a free-spawn coro handle; nothing frees it. Fix needs dispatcher-side surgery: a signal-or-reap path (bind the detached free-spawn handle to its slot; on the coroutine's completion slot-signal, if the bound handle is detached+unregistered, free handle+slot instead of just signalling — UAF-safe because a detached free-spawn handle has no joiner). Touches runtime/src/event_loop.rs (KaracParkSlot signal path) + src/codegen/coro.rs (route coro finish through the reap-aware signal). Must clear scripts/lsan-local.sh. Lower severity than the parent: tg.spawn is the documented/canonical server shape; free-spawn is the secondary variant. FIXED 2026-06-17 (69a03439): slot-armed self-reap. KaracParkSlot gained a type-erased `reap` pointer; karac_runtime_task_detach for a free-spawn coro handle calls karac_runtime_park_slot_arm_reap (under the slot `done` lock: either the coroutine already completed -> detach frees now, or store the handle for completion to free), and karac_runtime_park_slot_signal reads the armed handle under that lock and frees handle+slot via karac_runtime_reap_detached_coro_handle after releasing it. The `done` lock makes the arm/complete handshake claim the free exactly once; sound because signal is the slot's last use on every completion path (the codegen CoroContext.slot/cancel-edge invariant). For every non-armed slot (reap==null) signal is byte-for-byte unchanged. Tests: runtime unit detached_free_spawn_coro_reaps_when_{already_complete_at_detach,completion_follows_detach} (both orderings) + coro_e2e coroutine_discarded_free_spawn_self_reaps_under_asan over a real loopback connection with a 2s barrier so Linux LSan is a deterministic regression. Green: full coro_e2e (28), that E2E under Linux LSan, and the memory_sanitizer suite 263/263 (shared signal path unregressed). NOTE: writing the E2E surfaced a separate, orthogonal anomaly — moving a channel Sender into a free-spawn coroutine closes the channel before the send lands (recv got 0); sidestepped here with a sleep barrier; SUBSEQUENTLY FIXED the same day by 691117f6 (the coroutine owns its moved channel-end params, closing the channel only after the send), logged retroactively as B-2026-06-17-9. | 69a03439 |

| B-2026-06-17-5 | codegen | low | `mut ref T` params already carry LLVM `noalias` (emit_param_alias_attrs), but that rested on an exclusive-borrow guarantee NOT enforced at call sites until B-2026-06-17-6 -- so the pre-existing noalias was latently UNSOUND (f(mut v,mut v) compiled). B-2026-06-17-6 (1e0fe5ea) closes that, making mut-ref noalias sound; kata:37's solver written in its natural `mut ref Array[i64,N]` form (enabled by B-2026-06-17-1) now gets it. | B-2026-06-17-6 | ownership | high | Exclusive-borrow rule not enforced at call sites: `f(mut v, mut v)` (two simultaneous `mut ref` exclusive borrows of the SAME binding) and `f(mut v, v)` (exclusive + shared of the same binding) both compile, violating design.md's exclusive-borrow rule (a `mut ref T` is allowed only when no other borrow, shared or exclusive, of T is active -- the load-bearing soundness pin; split_at_mut is the sanctioned disjoint-partition path). The ownership checker accepts the aliasing under BOTH `karac run` and `karac build`. Worse, codegen then DIVERGES from the interpreter on the aliased case -- a latent miscompile: `fn f(x: mut ref Vec[i64], y: mut ref Vec[i64]) { x.push(1); y.push(2); println(x.len()); println(y.len()) }` with `f(mut v, mut v)` prints len(x)=2,len(y)=2 under `karac run` (true aliasing) but len(x)=1,len(y)=2 under `karac build` (codegen passes the Vec {ptr,len,cap} header by value per borrow, so x's len is stale). This is the BLOCKER for B-2026-06-17-5 (noalias): exclusive-borrow enforcement is the precondition that makes mut-param noalias sound (exactly the invariant Rust's &mut relies on). Surfaced by kata:37 while investigating the noalias gap. Fix: enforce the exclusive-borrow rule in the ownership checker -- reject a second active shared/exclusive borrow of a binding already exclusively borrowed at a call argument. | 1e0fe5ea |
| B-2026-06-17-7 | codegen | low | SOLVED (root cause identified + fixed): kata:37's solver ran ~1.34x behind Rust, and the earlier recharacterization left the cause 'unidentified'. IR/asm-level isolation of `go` pinned it: Rust FULLY UNROLLED the hot candidate loop `while d <= 9 { .. if go(..) ..; d = d + 1 }` while karac's default<O2> pipeline left it ROLLED -- and that single difference was the entire gap. Proven end-to-end: (1) C mirror + `#pragma clang loop unroll(full)` on the candidate loop lands EXACTLY on Rust (189.8ms) with 9 recursive bls; (2) rustc with -unroll-threshold=0 drops Rust back onto Kara/C at ~255ms (rolled). clang's cost model DECLINES this unroll (recursive call + early exit look expensive) even at -O3 -funroll-loops; rustc's LLVM config takes it. So Kara+C were at the correct 'rolled' floor; Rust uniquely unrolled. NB the prior bounds-check-elision hypothesis (B-2026-06-17-7 v1) and noalias hypothesis (B-2026-06-17-5) were both correctly refuted -- the cause was loop unrolling all along. FIX (1de4eb1e): emit `llvm.loop.unroll.full` metadata on the back-edge of small, constant-upper-bounded counted while loops (v < K / v <= K with a constant-step induction var, K <= 32), so LLVM's full unroller fires. Advisory-SAFE: unrolling is semantics-preserving and LLVM ignores the hint when it can't prove a small constant trip count. karac's first llvm.loop metadata emission (self-referential loop-id via temporary-node + RAUW through llvm-sys). RESULT: kata:37 Kara 254 -> 183ms, now 1.03-1.04x AHEAD of Rust (Kara carries noalias + no fixed-Array bounds checks; Rust's &mut [i64] slices still bounds-check). Cross-kata win: kata:36's 9-cell validator loops 192 -> 66ms (2.88x). Binary-search/permutation katas (variable-bounded loops) unchanged -- the gate is narrow by design. Tests: E2E rolled-vs-unrolled byte-identical output + IR gate (eligible loop carries the hint, large-bound loop does not). codegen 1611 / ownership 318 / typechecker 1692 green. | 1de4eb1e |

Root cause: the spawn wrapper only ramps the coroutine (which parks on accept) and returns; draining its channel-end cleanup frame (drain_top_frame_with_emit) closed the channel at ramp-return, before the coroutine's later resume ran tx.send. | B-2026-06-18-7 | codegen | low | `for c in s.chars()` called `karac_string_decode_char` PER CHARACTER to decode one UTF-8 scalar. | B-2026-06-18-8 | codegen | high | A heap value (String/Vec[T]) moved into a tg.spawn/spawn closure INSIDE A LOOP was freed twice (use-after-free / double-free): the spawn-capture move-suppression in lower_spawn_shared (src/codegen/task_group.rs) removed the parent's user-Drop (suppress_user_drop_for_var) and channel-end (suppress_channel_drop_for_var) cleanups but NOT its FreeVecBuffer. The {data,len,cap} header is bitwise-copied into the spawned task's heap capture env (the task now owns the buffer and frees it at completion), yet the parent ALSO freed it at loop-body scope exit -- racing the task that still reads it. A single non-loop spawn masks it because the TaskGroup join at the enclosing scope precedes the parent free; a loop drains each iteration's frame first. Affects both the coroutine and non-coroutine spawn paths (shared lower_spawn_shared capture loop). NOT cfg-gated -> platform-agnostic. Surfaced by the Relay dogfood (examples/relay/relay.kara) slice 2 round-robin load balancer: each accepted connection clones the next upstream address (String) out of a Vec and moves it into a per-connection tg.spawn handler in the accept loop; pre-fix the handler's TcpStream.connect received a freed/garbage address and the proxy returned empty responses for every request. Note: the bug was initially MIS-diagnosed as an ASAN-invisible 'deeper race' because grep/line-counting detectors miscounted concurrent unsynchronized println() output interleaving as memory corruption; a corruption-only detector (task compares its captured String to known content, prints only on mismatch) showed 0/960 corruption post-fix on both paths, and a 30-way concurrent Relay load test returned 30/30 balanced 10/10/10. Fix (6972ffb3): suppress_vec_buffer_drop_for_var (src/codegen/runtime.rs), a sibling of the user-Drop/channel-end suppressors, removes the parent's FreeVecBuffer by ALLOCA match (type-agnostic -- a String binding's slot type is not always the canonical vec-struct type), called in lower_spawn_shared's capture loop. Same family as B-2026-06-17-9 (a moved-into-spawn value freed by the wrong owner) but for plain heap collections rather than channel ends, and exposed by loop scope rather than a single spawn. Green: ASAN suite 263, coro_e2e 30, fmt + clippy clean. | B-2026-06-18-9 | codegen | high | `<expr>.clone()` on a `ref`/`mut ref` (BORROWED) collection receiver mis-built into a shallow ALIAS sharing the source buffer, while the interpreter always deep-copied -- a run/build divergence. `try_compile_clone` (src/codegen/entry_chains.rs) passed the receiver variable's raw alloca pointer (`src_slot.ptr`) to the per-type clone fn. Harmless inside allocation slack, but the push that fills an exact-size-class buffer (cap 64/128/256...) overflowed the allocation by those trailing bytes, corrupting the adjacent heap -> an ASLR-intermittent SIGSEGV on a later realloc/free once the buffer grew past ~64 elements. The pushed values read back CORRECT (consecutive overlapping wide stores each preserve their own low byte, and the final element's high bytes are zero), so it ran clean under the interpreter and printed the right answer in small programs; only large sub-word Vecs built with COMPUTED elements (e.g. `v.push(b'a' + (i as u8))`, the kata-44 wildcard bench terrain) crashed. Root cause: the element build_store in vec_method.rs (push / try_push / push_front / try_push_front) and collections.rs (compile_vec_index_store / compile_slice_index_store) wrote `elem_val` raw; the GEP and allocation correctly use the 1-byte elem stride/size, but a u8-typed expression that involves arithmetic or a cast compiles to i64, so the store width (driven by the value's LLVM type) was 8. | B-2026-06-19-6 | codegen | low | A read-only `let r = v[i]` binding of a HEAP-owning element out of a `Vec[Vec[T]]` (or any Vec whose element type is non-trivially-copyable) ALWAYS deep-clones the element, even when `r` is only read and never escapes — doubling allocation traffic on enumerate-then-scan workloads. Found via kata #46 (permutations): the n!-enumeration bench ran ~2x slower than C, and a malloc interposer pinned it to Kara issuing EXACTLY 2x C's allocations (10,080 vs 5,040 mallocs/solve at n=7). Decomposition: the append `out.push(path.clone())` is a correct SINGLE-alloc move (the clone buffer is moved in, source cap zeroed); the redundant second malloc+free per element is the signature loop's `let perm = perms[j]` — `clone_owned_vec_index_element` (collections.rs ~1478, called from the let arm in stmts.rs ~1779) deep-clones the shallow element so the binding owns a distinct buffer, guarding the alias double-free / dangling-after-container-drop class (B-2026-06-14-11, B-2026-06-18-9, the self-hosted-parser UAF). Confirmed: rewriting the read as a direct double-index `perms[j][i]` (no element binding) drops to 1 malloc/elem and matches C (verified: bound form 200,030 mallocs / direct form 100,030 over 100k iters). The clone is SEMANTICALLY required (an element cannot be moved out of a Vec by indexing) — eliminating it is an observational-equivalence optimization that needs a borrow-safety proof, so it sits at the documented v1 perf bar (design.md: 'within ~2x apples-to-apples') and is the roadmap's #1 lever ('allocation reduction on hot paths'). PLANNED FIX (clone-elision): at the `let r = v[i]` site, bind `r` as a shallow borrow (alias the element buffer) and suppress r's scope-exit FreeVecBuffer, gated on a conservative whitelist lexical scan over r's scope (rest of enclosing block + nested blocks) proving (a) r is an immutable simple binding, (b) the element type is heap-owning, (c) r appears only in read positions — index-read, `.len()`/`.is_empty()`, never a call/own-arg/return/assign/non-read-method/composite-literal (the use-classifier's never-Consumed signal corroborates), (d) the container v appears only as index-reads in r's scope (no mutating method, assign, index-store, by-value move — any v.push reallocs and would dangle r), (e) no closure literal in r's scope. Any uncertainty falls back to the existing clone (false-negatives are free; only false-positives are UAF, so the gate is whitelist-only). Regression must include adversarial NEGATIVE cases that MUST still clone+stay correct: mutate-r-after-bind, return/store/own-arg escape of r, `v.push` after the bind, closure capturing v, shadow-rebind of r/v — run under Linux ASAN+LSan (sanitizers have missed this class before, so build+run E2E + adversarial coverage, not sanitizer-alone). FIXED: added a conservative whitelist borrow-elision pre-pass (src/codegen/borrow_elision.rs, compute_vec_index_borrow_spans, run per fn in compile_function). It marks a `let r = v[i]` RHS span borrow-safe only when, over r's lexical scope (the rest of the enclosing block + nested blocks), every use of r is a recognised read (index-read, .len()/.is_empty(), never a call/own-arg/return/assign/non-read-method/composite-literal) AND v appears only as index-reads (no mutating method, assign, index-store, by-value move) AND there is no closure and no shadow-rebind of r/v; ANY unrecognised construct disqualifies (whitelist-only, so only false-NEGATIVES are possible — never an unsafe borrow). The Let arm (stmts.rs) then skips clone_owned_vec_index_element AND the binding's scope-exit track_vec_* (FreeVecBuffer + recursive drop) for marked spans, so r aliases the element and the container stays the unique owner. Result: the kata-46 read loop drops from 2 mallocs/elem to 1 (matches C); the n!=5040 enumeration's allocation traffic halves. Tests: tests/codegen.rs borrow_elision_elides_read_only_vecvec_index_binding (IR: read-loop clone gone), borrow_elision_keeps_clone_for_unsafe_index_bindings (IR: overwrite/escape/grow/callarg negatives all RETAIN the clone), e2e_borrow_elision_correctness_positive_and_negatives (build+run), and tests/memory_sanitizer.rs asan_borrow_elision_read_only_vecvec_index_is_clean + asan_borrow_elision_escape_negative_clones_and_is_clean (ASAN: no UAF/double-free; Linux CI LSan covers the leak arm). Minimal repro: `fn main() { let mut out: Vec[Vec[i64]] = Vec.new(); let mut b: Vec[i64] = Vec.new(); b.push(5i64); let mut k=0i64; while k<4i64 { out.push(b.clone()); k=k+1i64; } let mut nb: Vec[i64] = Vec.new(); nb.push(99i64); out[0i64] = nb; println(f"{out[0i64][0i64]}") }` → exit 133 built, '99' interpreted. FIXED: the index-store path now (a) drops the OLD heap element before overwriting and (b) suppresses the moved source binding's scope-exit cleanup. compile_vec_index_store (collections.rs) calls emit_free_vec_buffer_if_owned(elem_ptr) when llvm_ty_is_vec_struct(elem_ty) — freeing the orphaned old buffer (outer-only, matching the Identifier-assign move-overwrite eager free; a live per-element alias keeps its own cleanup, and borrow-elision B-2026-06-19-6 refuses to alias when the container is index-stored in scope, so the freed slot has no borrowed reader). The Index-assign arm in stmts.rs then calls suppress_source_vec_cleanup_for_arg(value) for an OWNING Vec target with a heap-struct element (gated off slice/map element stores), zeroing the moved source's cap so only the container frees the buffer — the same move discipline as Vec.push and the Identifier-assign path. Verified: `out[j]=nb` (single + 10k-loop), fresh call-result RHS, and Vec[String] elements all build+run exit 0 with a flat alloc balance (no per-iteration leak). Tests: tests/codegen.rs e2e_index_store_heap_vec_element_no_double_free + e2e_index_store_heap_string_element_no_double_free (build+run, crash regression); tests/memory_sanitizer.rs asan_index_store_heap_vec_element_no_double_free (ASAN clean; Linux CI LSan covers the leak arm). | — |
| B-2026-06-19-8 | codegen | high | Vec.filled(n, val) with a heap-backed element type bit-copied the SAME fill aggregate into all N slots, so every slot aliased one backing buffer: the canonical 2D DP table `let dp: Vec[Vec[i64]] = Vec.filled(rows, Vec.filled(cols, x))` corrupted across rows on write and N-fold-freed the shared buffer on drop (AOT exit 133 / SIGTRAP). `karac run` (interpreter) was correct (it deep-copies rows), so codegen-only. Surfaced by the cross-kata canonical-idiom audit (DP family: kata #10/#44/#91 edit-distance/wildcard/decode-ways tables). The pre-existing safe case `Vec.filled(n, Vec.new())` works only because the empty `{null,0,0}` aggregate has no buffer to alias. FIXED: build_vec_filled (collections.rs) now deep-clones per slot for non-trivially-copyable element types — it moves `val` into slot 0 and emit_clone_fn_for_type_expr-clones it into slots 1..n (the `vec![x;n]` discipline: N distinct buffers, `val` consumed, no extra drop, no variable-arg double-free). The destination element TypeExpr is threaded from the let binding via a new `pending_let_elem_type_expr` field (the TypeExpr sibling of pending_let_elem_type), CONSUMED at the start of the `filled` arm before the fill argument is compiled so a nested inner Vec.filled(...) does not inherit the outer binding's element type. Trivial element types (i64, flat structs) keep the bit-copy path. Residual: an un-annotated nested-collection fill (no TypeExpr to recover) and 3D+ nesting fall back to bit-copy (no worse than before; 2D + annotated is the canonical case). | B-2026-06-19-9 | interpreter+codegen | med | Structural `==`/`!=` on a `shared struct` (design.md § Equality Semantics) was unhandled in both backends despite a correct `#[derive(Eq, PartialEq)]`. | B-2026-06-19-11 | codegen | high | A heap value (Vec[T] / String) captured READ-ONLY by MULTIPLE sibling TaskGroup.spawn tasks while the parent still owns it — the canonical parallel-stencil fan-out `for band: tg.spawn(|| f(grid, lo, hi))` where the closures pass the shared buffer to a `ref` param — was miscompiled: the blocking-spawn lowering in codegen/task_group.rs treated EVERY capture as a by-move transfer, so each task re-registered a free of the captured {data,len,cap} buffer (lower_spawn_shared's FreeVecBuffer re-registration) AND the parent's scope-exit free was suppressed. With N tasks capturing the one shared buffer, it was freed N times — a double-free / use-after-free. Symptoms: wrong results (a 4-task band-sum of 0..99 returned 328/332 instead of 4950, non-deterministic) and an allocator abort 'failed to lock mutex: Invalid argument (os error 22)'. Reading only the copied scalar header field (data.len()) was fine; only dereferencing the shared buffer corrupted. The cross-task-safe check (cross_task_safe.rs) did not catch it — plain Vec/String are not on the five-leaf unsafe list and the body's *type* is safe; the flaw was the lowering's ownership assumption, not the capture type. Moving a unique buffer into one task (each task owns its own) always worked. ROOT: spawn lowering ignored the ownership pass's per-capture mode (closure_capture_paths / OwnershipMode), which par {} branches already honor (ParCaptureMode::Copy: a shared Vec read across branches is passed by value, parent frees once after the join barrier). FIX: lower_spawn_shared now classifies each captured root as borrow (every path Ref/MutRef) vs move (any Own); a borrowed capture on the blocking path neither re-registers the wrapper-side free nor suppresses the parent's free, so the parent frees the buffer exactly once after the structured-concurrency join barrier — the design.md Structured Concurrency Lifetime Guarantees borrow ('a parallel task may legally borrow a binding ... the task joins strictly before the cleanup fires'). Moves and the coroutine-spawn path keep the by-value transfer. This also resolves the latent leak the suppress-only B-2026-06-18-8 fix left for a single borrowed capture (parent now frees it). Tests: tests/memory_sanitizer.rs asan_taskgroup_spawn_shared_vec_read_across_tasks_single_free + asan_taskgroup_spawn_shared_string_read_across_tasks_single_free (value correctness 4950/hits-3 + ASAN no-double-free; Linux LSan covers the leak arm — verified green via scripts/lsan-local.sh taskgroup_spawn, all 6 incl. the existing move/loop-borrow cases). | — |
| B-2026-06-19-12 | typechecker+interpreter+codegen | med | Two width-dependent integer scalar method families were unrecognized (`no method 'pow'/'count_ones' on type ...`), surfaced by the cross-kata math-bit audit (Tier-A A1/A3). FIXED complete across all three backends. (1) `n.pow(k) -> Self`: repeated-multiply power, exponent is `u32` (Rust's `iN::pow(self, exp: u32)`; suffix-free literal promotes, otherwise must be u32 with an `as u32` hint), traps `integer overflow` at the receiver width exactly as the `*` it iterates. Interpreter (method_call.rs eval_int_pow) uses square-and-multiply with i128 range checks (the squared base can't false-trap because its exponent 2^k <= exp); codegen (codegen/method_call.rs) emits a counted loop whose body reuses emit_checked_int_arith("mul",..) so an out-of-range partial product traps at the declared width. (2) `count_ones`/`leading_zeros`/`trailing_zeros` -> u32: width-correct (count within the receiver's declared bits; a signed iN is masked to width first, so i8 -1 has 8 set bits and u8 0 has 8 leading/trailing zeros, NOT the i64-widened 64). Codegen lowers to llvm.ctpop/ctlz/cttz on the narrowed iN (ctlz/cttz with is_zero_poison=false → bit-width on zero, matching Rust/interp). WIDTH RECOVERY: both families need the declared receiver width, but a MethodCall's Expr.span aliases its receiver span and the generic infer_expr post-record clobbers expr_types[receiver.span] with the call's result type (Self for pow — harmless — but u32 for the bit intrinsics). Fix: thread the non-aliased args_close_span (the `)` leaf) into infer_method_call + eval_method_call; the typechecker stashes the receiver type there and the interpreter reads it back clobber-free. Codegen (which has no general expr_types and gets only call_span) recovers width from the existing method_callee_types["<recv>.<method>"] record with a clobber-detection fallback to the receiver's declared type / literal suffix, then operates at that width and re-extends the result to the i64-backed representation narrow ints flow in. | B-2026-06-19-14 | codegen | high | SoA `layout` blocks did not cross function boundaries — passing a SoA-laid-out Vec[E] to another function miscompiled. The layout makes the binding-site a 4-field SoA value {g0_ptr,...,len,cap} (soa_layouts is a name-keyed codegen map), but a callee's `Vec[E]` parameter is always compiled with the default AoS {ptr,len,cap} representation, and the SoA access paths GEP the param's slot alloca directly. By-VALUE: caller loads the 4-field SoA and passes it to a 3-field AoS param -> LLVM 'Call parameter type does not match function signature' verification failure (loud). By-REF (`ref Vec[E]`): the slot alloca holds a POINTER to the caller's SoA struct, but compile_soa_index_read / compile_soa_method GEP'd the alloca as if it were the struct -> reads the pointer's bytes as group-ptrs/len -> garbage len (e.g. 1073741824) -> SIGTRAP (exit 133). A SILENT miscompile. AoS (no layout block) is correct; single-function SoA (push/index/field/len all within the declaring fn) is correct. Surfaced by the Slipstream LBM dogfood (examples/slipstream): its kernel splits the grid across `ref Vec[LbmNode]` helpers (collide_band/stream_band/velocities/render_fb), so it could not use SoA at all -- exactly the 'SoA layout' capability the roster bills it on. PARTIAL FIX: the by-REF READ path now works. compile_soa_index_read (collections.rs) and compile_soa_method (exprs.rs) compute a `soa_struct_ptr` that derefs the slot alloca once when the binding is a `ref`/`mut ref` param (self.ref_params), so the callee operates on the caller's existing SoA struct; a by-value/`let` binding's slot already IS the struct (no deref). (4) Tail-CALL SoA-return propagation -- a SoA-returning fn whose body ENDS IN a layout-returning call (substep's fan_stream(coll,..)) returned AoS while its signature was SoA; compile_tail_final_expr flows the return layout to the tail call. | B-2026-06-20-1 | codegen | med | Passing a bare named `fn` as a first-class `Fn(...)` value miscompiles. `fn apply(f: Fn(i64)->i64, x: i64) -> i64 { f(x) }` called as `apply(doubler, 21)` (doubler a named fn) parses + type-checks fine, but codegen lowers `TypeKind::FnType` to the default `i64` (types_lowering.rs llvm_type_for_type_expr falls through) while a bare fn name lowers to a raw `ptr` (exprs.rs free-fn-as-value), so the higher-order call fails LLVM module verification: 'Call parameter type does not match function signature! ptr @doubler ... call i64 @apply(ptr @doubler, i64 21)'. Only the special-cased `Server.serve(handler)` dispatch works today (landed 2026-05-09, commit 60ce3a4); the general `Fn`-typed-parameter path is unsupported and was untracked. Workaround: wrap in a closure (`apply(|x| doubler(x), 21)`), which builds the {fn_ptr,env} fat pointer. Fix = lower FnType to the closure fat-pointer struct {ptr,ptr} and reify a bare fn name into {ptr, null-env} at Fn-typed arg sites (or have the Fn ABI accept a raw ptr). Surfaced writing the `#[inline(always)]`-through-fn-value IR test for the codegen-hint-attrs slice (phase-8-stdlib-floor.md line 775); the attribute itself emits correctly regardless of call shape, so only the indirect-call test is blocked. | B-2026-06-20-2 | typechecker+interpreter+codegen | med | Four allocating String->String methods were unrecognized (Tier-B B1): `trim()` / `to_lowercase()` / `to_uppercase()` (no-arg -> String) and `replace(from, to)` (two String args -> String). FIXED complete across all three backends with FULL UNICODE semantics matching Rust's str stdlib exactly — `to_lowercase`/`to_uppercase` are Unicode case maps that can CHANGE byte length (`straße`.to_uppercase() == `STRASSE`), `trim` strips Unicode whitespace, `replace` is byte-substring. Typechecker (stdlib_seq.rs infer_str_method): arg-shape validation + String result. Interpreter (method_call_seq.rs try_eval_seq_method): direct Rust `s.trim().to_string()` / `s.to_lowercase()` / `s.to_uppercase()` / `s.replace(from,to)`. NOTE the interpreter `replace` arm is String-guarded and the vector handler (try_eval_vector_method, SIMD `Vector.replace`) runs BEFORE the seq handler, so a Vector receiver never reaches the new String arm. CODEGEN: new runtime helpers in runtime/src/clone.rs — `karac_string_{to_lowercase,to_uppercase,trim}(data, len, *mut out_len) -> ptr` and `karac_string_replace(data, len, from, from_len, to, to_len, *mut out_len) -> ptr`, each computing the result via the SAME Rust stdlib call as the interpreter (so the two backends are bit-identical on Unicode without shipping Unicode tables into codegen) and returning a fresh NUL-terminated `{ptr, out_len, out_len}` (cap==len) buffer (null+0 for empty, the karac_string_slice convention). codegen.rs declares the 4 externs; vec_method.rs adds the dispatch arms (load receiver {data,len}, extract arg {ptr,len} pairs, call helper with an out_len alloca, build the String aggregate via the shared build_string_xform_result helper). The result is freed exactly once by the existing String scope-cleanup registration (same path as repeat/slice). Decision: full Unicode (not an ASCII-only shortcut) — an ASCII `to_lowercase` would be a silent correctness footgun on non-ASCII AND would diverge from the interpreter's Rust-Unicode result. trim allocates an OWNED copy rather than returning a borrowed view (a String-view story is a future optimization). ROOT CAUSE: compile_field_store had no SoA branch, so `bodies[i].x = expr` fell into the nested-plain-struct path which treats the SoA struct as a contiguous AoS element — it read the SoA header's field-0 pointer as the data base and strided by the FULL element size. Index 0 coincidentally hit group-0 slot 0; index >= 1 wrote PAST the group buffer (a silent heap overflow), so the store was dropped. Repro (single function, no call boundary): struct Body { x: f64, vx: f64, health: f64 }; layout bodies: Vec[Body] { group pos { x } group vel { vx } group hp { health } }; push two elements, then `bodies[0].x = 7.0; bodies[1].x = 9.0; println(bodies[0].x + bodies[1].x)`. Codegen (SoA) prints 17; the AoS interpreter oracle prints 16. The field-level SoA index-store writes element index 0 correctly but the store at index 1 lands at neither slot 1 nor slot 0 (read-back of bodies[0].x is still 7, bodies[1].x is still its original 10) -- the per-group destination address is computed wrong for index >= 1 (likely a missing index*elem_stride term / wrong group base, mirroring nothing like compile_soa_index_read's correct read addressing), so non-zero-index field scatters are effectively dropped. Pure cross-group READS (bodies[i].x + bodies[i].health) are correct (covered by existing tests). PRE-EXISTING: the base compiler at 6296b9ae miscompiles it byte-identically, so it is NOT introduced by per-layout-mono slice 5 (db584a09, which only swapped the layout value carrier). Independent of the borrow checker (a codegen address-arithmetic fault, not an aliasing-fact gap; surfaced while auditing cross-group disjointness for the e.position += e.velocity idiom). Same family as the unbuilt whole-element index-store grid[i] = E{..} (still open). UNBLOCKS B-2026-06-19-14 slice 6 (Slipstream's LBM kernel scatters field updates by index). |

The Map.remove arm's existing incoming-key free (free_fresh_owned_str_arg, B-2026-06-20-9) is unchanged and complementary: it releases the key ARGUMENT on the no-adopt path; the new drop_key releases the STORED key the bucket adopted at insert. | B-2026-06-20-13 | codegen | high | Heap `for`-loop element BORROW consumed by a retaining sink double-freed in codegen (A/B mismatch on the flagship counter idiom). `for w in vec` over a Vec is BORROW-iteration: the loop binds `w` to an ALIAS of `data[i]` (a plain header load, compile_for_vec_var) and the source Vec RETAINS ownership — it is usable after the loop (`for w in words {..}; words.len()` works, prints the full count). So a consume site that RETAINS `w` — `m.entry(w)`, `v.push(w)`, `m.insert(w, ..)` — bit-copied `w`'s `{ptr,len,cap}` into the sink, and BOTH the sink's drop and the source Vec's scope-exit drop freed the same buffer (double-free; SIGTRAP, buffered stdout lost). The interpreter clones values freely (GC-by-Value-clone), so it produced the right answer — this was a silent A/B divergence on the canonical histogram `for w in words { *m.entry(w).or_insert(0) += 1 }` (codegen crashed; interp printed the counts). Earlier mis-diagnosed as entry-specific (B-2026-06-20-11 RELATED note) because the `push(w)` control used STRING LITERAL elements (cap==0 rodata — no heap to double-free); with `.to_string()` heap elements, push/insert double-free identically. So it is general to all retaining-consume sites, not entry. FIX (codegen, no runtime change): a new `for_loop_borrow_vars` set marks heap (String/Vec) for-loop element bindings — `register_for_loop_bindings` adds a Binding (and the k/v of `for (k,v) in m`) when the element landed in `vec_elem_types` (the {ptr,len,cap} shapes) via the new `mark_for_loop_borrow_if_heap`. `maybe_defensive_copy_param_arg` treats membership the SAME as `owned_vecstr_params`: it deep-copies the borrowed element (`emit_vecstr_defensive_copy`) so the sink owns a private buffer while the source Vec keeps freeing its own elements — exactly the owned-param model, one level in (the source retains the scope-exit free in both). The consume sites (Vec.push/push_back, Map.insert key+value, the entry-chain key from B-2026-06-20-9) already call that helper, so they are fixed by the gate change alone; read-only loop bodies never call it, so they are untouched (no extra clone). A later `let` of the same name clears stale membership in the binding-registration block (shadow guard) so a fresh owned binding reusing a loop var name is not wrongly copied (the copy pairs with a source-suppress → would orphan the fresh String; LSan-only). Cleared per-function alongside `owned_vecstr_params`; NOT mono-saved (parity with owned_vecstr_params, which also relies on the per-fn clear). A/B verified byte-identical: the canonical word-frequency kata (histogram via `for w in words { *freq.entry(w)... }`, ascending report) now matches under `karac run` and `karac build`. | B-2026-06-20-14 | codegen | high | Three PRE-EXISTING leaks the Linux-LSan gate (scripts/lsan-local.sh) flags but the macOS post-landing ASAN run misses (Apple clang has no LeakSanitizer), surfaced by the phase-12 self-host render slices and confirmed failing on clean main. NOT introduced by the B-2026-06-20-9 map-key fix (all three are non-map). (1) SHARED-ENUM String/Vec payload MOVE-OUT double-free (suppress_shared_enum_payload_move_out, control_flow_match.rs). `match e { S(s) => s }` over `shared enum E { S(String) }` (the render_expr/get shape, returned) only zeroed the LOCAL binding's cap on move-out via the tail-move logic -- the RC box's payload words still pointed at the moved-out buffer, so the box's `__karac_rc_drop_<E>` (whose Vec/String arm frees cap>0) re-freed it after the caller already freed the returned String: a double-free (macOS ASAN catches it; the nested tests-1/2 form only LEAKED because the boxed-struct-drop gap below masked it -- the inner box's drop never ran). Fix: the shared sibling of the existing suppress_destructured_enum_payload_cleanup_at, which explicitly bails on layout.is_shared. For each consumed EnumDropKind::VecOrString field, zero its payload words IN THE BOX (heap index start_word+2, mirroring emit_shared_enum_rc_drop_fn) so the box rc-drop skips the buffer the binding now owns. Gated to owned (non-borrow) shared scrutinees; shared-handle (rc-managed) and NestedStruct payloads are untouched. (2) SHARED-ENUM BOXED-struct payload rc-drop gap (emit_shared_enum_field_drop boxed arm + emit_nested_struct_shared_rc_decs_ex, synth_drop.rs). A struct payload wider than its allotted payload-area words is heap-boxed at construction (coerce_to_payload_words, `out.len() > num_words`: e.g. `struct Block { tail: Option[Expr] }` used as `Expr.Blk(Block)` -- the Option field hits the enum-in-enum carve-out, undersizing the area while Block is 4 words), but the rc-drop's struct arm ALWAYS read the payload INLINE -- GEP'ing the box-POINTER word as the struct's first field (a garbage tag, so the recursion skipped) and never freeing the box. Fix: recompute the SAME `llvm_type_word_count(struct) > num_words` predicate the pack/unpack sites use, and on boxed: inttoptr word 0 -> heap struct, walk it, then free the box. The walk passes nested_buffer_free=Some(false) (a new param replacing the old recurse bool): the boxed struct's DIRECT Vec/String buffers + shared/Option[shared] children are reclaimed, but a NESTED heap struct FIELD (`IfNode.then_block: Block`) is recursed to rc-dec ONLY its RC children -- because that nested struct may be MOVED OUT by the match binding (`let tb = nd.then_block`), whose own __karac_drop_struct_<S> value-drop frees its BUFFERS but does NOT rc-dec its shared children. Re-freeing those buffers through the box walk was a double-free (regressed tests/codegen.rs::test_e2e_shared_enum_payload_with_nested_heap_struct_field -> empty output: a SIGSEGV at the scope-exit drop lost the buffered stdout); skipping the children was a leak. Some(false) splits them: buffers to the move-out owner, RC children to the box -- no double-free, no stranded child. RESIDUAL BOUNDED LEAK (documented v1, never corruption): a NEVER-moved-out nested heap struct's own Vec/String buffer inside a boxed payload is not reclaimed (the box walk leaves nested buffers to a move-out owner that, in that case, does not exist); none of the suite hits this. (3) METHOD-CALL fresh String/Vec temp arg leak (compile_method_call, method_call.rs). A fresh String/Vec produced by a Call/MethodCall and passed DIRECTLY by value to a USER method (`lx.ident_matches("Fn".to_string())`) had no consuming binding, and an owned by-value Vec/String param is NOT freed by the callee (it lands in owned_vecstr_params for retaining-consume deep-copy, never a callee-side track_vec_var) -- so the temp orphaned, leaking one buffer per call. The free-fn compile_call arg loop already materializes such args into a caller-scope __owned_tmp with a scope-exit free (the #20 is_fresh_heap_call_arg arm + the bare-shared __owned_arg_tmp arm); the method arg loop was missing it. Fix: mirror both arms verbatim after track_inline_owned_aggregate_arg, with the same guards (expr_yields_fresh_owned_temp / inline-temp-vec-index, llvm_ty_is_vec_struct, !rhs_stages_fstr_acc). Built-in consuming methods (push/insert/entry.or_insert) are special-cased BEFORE this generic user-method dispatch, so they are unaffected (verified: or_insert(Vec.new()) emits no __owned_tmp). Tests: tests/codegen.rs +3 IR-shape (shared_enum_string_payload_moveout_zeros_box_cap; shared_enum_boxed_struct_payload_rc_drop_unboxes_and_frees; method_call_fresh_string_temp_arg_materialized); tests/memory_sanitizer.rs +2 E2E (asan_shared_enum_string_payload_moveout_no_double_free -- the minimal move-out double-free that no prior test isolated, all existing shared-enum tests extract only scalar/shared-handle payloads; asan_shared_enum_boxed_struct_payload_moveout_no_double_free -- the boxed-struct nested-move-out, LSan-clean). | B-2026-06-20-15 | typechecker+codegen | medium | Set[Vec[T]] (and Map[Vec[T], _]) did not deduplicate equal-CONTENTS vecs -- two equal vecs inserted as distinct elements (len()==2 instead of 1), an A/B divergence vs the interpreter (which dedupes via structural Value::Array eq). A `Set` has HashSet value semantics, so this is a correctness bug. Two Vec-specific causes: (1) the built-in `Vec` is registered with no derived traits so type_supports_hash/eq reported it un-Hash/un-Eq -- a hard ERROR in the codegen path (Set[Vec[T]] never compiled) but only a warning in the interpreter path; (2) past that gate, codegen's Vec element hash/eq used the byte-loop fallback over the {ptr,len,cap} HEADER (pointer identity) instead of walking the contents. String elements always deduped (byte-walk arm), masking the gap. Discovered while writing the B-2026-06-20-12 Set incoming-element leak tests (efeb9dbf); the leak fix is unrelated and already landed -- this is the separate functional dedup gap flagged there. | ddc625ad. TWO Vec-specific root causes, both fixed. (1) TYPECHECKER (src/typechecker/derives.rs): the built-in `Vec` is registered in env.structs with NO derived traits, so `type_supports_hash`/`type_supports_eq` fell through to the generic `Type::Named` lookup and reported `Vec` as un-Hash/un-Eq -- a HARD ERROR in the codegen (`karac build`) path (so `Set[Vec[T]]` did not even compile) but only a non-fatal WARNING in the interpreter (`karac run`) path (interpreter is GC-by-Value-clone and dedupes via structural `Value::Array` eq, so it printed the right answer). Fix: a dedicated `Type::Named { name: "Vec", args } if args.len()==1` arm in BOTH predicates, placed BEFORE the generic Named struct/enum lookup, that recurses into the element (`Vec[T]` is Hash/Eq by content iff `T` is) -- mirrors the existing `Type::Array`/`Type::Slice`/`Type::Vector` recursion and `type_supports_display`'s explicit `"Vec"` arm. `Set[Vec[f64]]` stays correctly REJECTED (f64 is not Eq -- IEEE-754 NaN!=NaN). (2) CODEGEN (src/codegen/synth.rs): even past that gate, a `Vec[T]` element/key routed through the `emit_hash_fn_for_type`/`emit_eq_fn_for_type` byte-loop FALLBACK, which hashes/compares the {ptr,len,cap} HEADER (pointer identity), so two equal-contents vecs land in different buckets and never collapse. (String elements always deduped via the `type_name=="String"` byte-walk arm, masking the gap.) Fix: a `Vec` dispatch arm in `emit_hash_fn_for_type_expr`/`emit_eq_fn_for_type_expr` (before the user-struct arm) that, for a `TypeKind::Path` head "Vec" with a `GenericArg::Type` arg, calls the new `emit_hash_fn_for_vec`/`emit_eq_fn_for_vec`; absent the arg it falls back to the header byte-loop. `emit_hash_fn_for_vec` emits `karac_hash_Vec_<elem>(*const Vec)->i64`: loads {data,len} from the {ptr,len,cap} header, seeds the FxHash state with `len` (length is part of the digest, matching Rust's `Hash for [T]`; rotate_left(0,5)=0 collapses mix(0,len) to len*SEED), then folds each per-element hash (`emit_hash_fn_for_type_expr(elem)`, recurses for Vec[String]/Vec[Vec[_]]) via the same rotate-5/xor/mul tail-mix the tuple/struct combiners use. `emit_eq_fn_for_vec` emits `karac_eq_Vec_<elem>(*const Vec,*const Vec)->i1`: compare lengths, then each element via the per-element eq fn, short-circuit false on first mismatch. CRITICAL naming: keyed on the element-aware `karac_hash_Vec_<elem>`/`karac_eq_Vec_<elem>` (via `display_mangle_te`) NOT the shallow `mangled_type_name` "Vec" -- otherwise distinct element types would share one now-content-dependent body; the dispatcher's early cache check (keyed on shallow "Vec") simply misses for Vec and the real dedup happens inside the new fns. Empty vecs: len 0 -> no element loop, hash 0, eq true (data ptr loaded but never dereferenced -> no NULL deref). `cap` is NOT read (a Vec's value identity is len+contents, not capacity). NO runtime/ABI change, NO archive rebuild, NO interpreter change (A/B byte-identical). Fixes `Map[Vec[T], _]` keys and Vec-field-bearing struct/tuple keys for free (all route through the same dispatchers). Vec-ONLY on BOTH sides (not VecDeque): the codegen content path is keyed on a Path head "Vec", so admitting VecDeque in the typechecker without a matching codegen path would re-create the A/B divergence one layer down -- keeping both sides Vec-only stays in lockstep. The fix ALSO opens a previously-UNREACHABLE ownership path: once two equal-contents vecs collapse, the second insert takes `karac_map_insert_old`'s EXISTS branch, whose incoming-element free (B-2026-06-20-12) now actually fires -- covered by a new LSan regression. TESTS: 3 codegen E2E (tests/codegen.rs: test_e2e_set_vec_dedup_by_content [dedup + distinct-stay-separate + contains/remove + same-prefix-diff-length non-equality], test_e2e_set_string_dedup_companion, test_e2e_map_vec_key_dedup_by_content); 2 typechecker (tests/typechecker.rs: test_set_and_map_accept_vec_element_when_inner_hash_eq, test_set_rejects_vec_element_when_inner_not_hash_eq); 1 LSan (tests/memory_sanitizer.rs: asan_set_vec_duplicate_element_dedup_no_leak_no_double_free, >=48-byte buffer per the LSan-reachability rule). | B-2026-06-20-16 | concurrency | high | Auto-par (statement-level) RACED a map-mutating loop against a later read of the same map under the DEFAULT `karac build` — a silent wrong-answer/crash. The word-frequency kata's `for w in words { *freq.entry(w).or_insert(0) += 1 }` histogram loop and the subsequent `freq.keys()` were placed in the SAME parallel_group (`--concurrency-report`: "no data or effect dependencies"), so `freq.keys()` ran concurrently while the loop was still mutating `freq` — a read-after-write race on the map (mutex panics, garbled output). `karac run` (interpreter) and `KARAC_AUTO_PAR=0 karac build` were both correct, so it was a silent A/B mismatch on the flagship counter idiom. ROOT CAUSE (src/concurrency.rs): the dual-analysis dependency graph builds per-statement reads/writes sets. `collect_assign_target_defines` (the write-target place-root resolver) matched only `Identifier` / `SelfValue` / `FieldAccess` / `Index` — it had NO arm for a `Unary{Deref}` or a `MethodCall` target, so a `*<place> = …` / `*<place> += …` whose place is a method chain recorded NO write. The CompoundAssign `*freq.entry(w).or_insert(0) += 1` therefore contributed zero writes; the `for`-loop's writes set (collected from the body via collect_block_inner_writes -> collect_assign_target_defines) omitted `freq`; the loop statement looked write-free; and the parallelizer saw no write-vs-read conflict with `freq.keys()` -> grouped -> raced. FIX: `collect_assign_target_defines` now recurses a `Unary{op: Deref}` target into its operand and a `MethodCall` place target into its receiver, so a write through a deref/method-chain roots at the underlying container — `*m.entry(k).or_insert(d) += 1` records writes(m), `*v.get_mut(i) = x` records writes(v). For a plain `*ref += …` on a mut-ref local it records the binding (the pointee's owner), which is conservative — it may over-serialize but NEVER under-serializes, the only safe direction for the parallel-safety gate. Reads were already captured (collect_block_reads routes CompoundAssign/Assign targets through the general collect_expr_reads, which recurses MethodCall/Unary). After the fix the racy loop+keys() parallel_group no longer forms (`--concurrency-report` shows only the two genuinely-independent groups), and the DEFAULT auto-par build of the word-frequency kata is A/B byte-identical to `karac run`. Tests: tests/concurrency.rs unit (a map-mutating loop is not co-grouped with a later `m.keys()` read) + tests/par_codegen.rs E2E (auto-par histogram-then-keys, deterministic sorted output — exercises the whole word-frequency cascade: moved-loop-element copy B-2026-06-20-13, keys deep-copy + String sort B-2026-06-20-11, and this serialization). Full concurrency unit suite 100, clippy --all --all-targets --features llvm + fmt clean. NO runtime change, NO archive rebuild. FOURTH and final gap surfaced by the bespoke word-frequency kata (after B-2026-06-20-9 entry/get/insert no-adopt, -11 sort+keys deep-copy, -13 moved-loop-element copy); the kata now runs A/B-clean under run + default build + KARAC_AUTO_PAR=0. | 1ee2b64d |

| B-2026-06-22-2 | codegen | high | An ESCAPING capturing closure silently miscompiles (dangling stack environment) — soundness hole surfaced finishing first-class fn values (B-2026-06-20-1..B-2026-06-21-3). A closure that captures a local and then outlives its defining frame — returned (`fn make(k: i64) -> Fn(i64)->i64 { |x| x + k }`), or stored in a struct field / Vec / global that escapes — reads its captures from freed stack memory after the frame returns. Repro: `fn make(k){ |x| x + k }; let f = make(10); println(f(5))` typechecks with 0 errors and `karac build` prints -1 (garbage) instead of 15; it is a WRONG-OUTPUT miscompile, not a verifier error or a diagnostic. Root cause: compile_closure (src/codegen/closures.rs) builds the env as a stack alloca in the OUTER fn frame (`create_entry_alloca(outer_fn, "__closure_env", ..)`) and the fat pointer's env slot points at it; there is NO heap allocation, NO escape analysis, and NO closure-env drop machinery anywhere today (a non-escaping closure is fine because the frame is still live when it's called, which is why all existing closure tests — same-frame `let f = |x| x+base; f(5)` — pass). Non-capturing escaping closures are safe (null env). The interpreter (`karac run`) is unaffected (tree-walk closures own their captured environment). FIX = the heap-closure-environment epic (tracked in phase-7-codegen.md as a sequenced plan): heap-allocate an escaping closure's env, drop POD then heap (String/Vec) captures at the owning value's scope exit, handle a closure value copied to multiple owners (RC env or strict move + move-out suppression), and add escape analysis so non-escaping closures keep the cheap stack env. Interim-safety option (if a slice can't land): reject a not-yet-supported escaping capturing closure with a clear `not yet supported` diagnostic so no silent miscompile remains. Until fixed, the workaround is to not return / store a capturing closure (pass it down by `Fn(..)` parameter instead, which keeps the defining frame live — already supported). PROGRESS — Slice 0 of the epic landed 2026-06-22 (ab6ff88b): reject_escaping_capturing_closure (a pure-AST pre-check at the top of compile_function) now turns the silent miscompile into an honest `error[E_ESCAPING_CLOSURE_NOT_YET]` for the common TAIL-position escape — a capturing-closure literal, or an identifier bound to one, in the function's tail / return (recursing through block/if/match tails). Sound programs are untouched (non-capturing closures, same-frame use, pass-down-by-Fn-param all still compile — full codegen suite 1743/0). Slice 0 EXTENDED 2026-06-22 (c006ccda): the guard now also covers an explicit mid-body `return <capturing closure>` (collect_outer_return_values walks every `return` not inside a nested closure) and a capturing closure returned inside an aggregate literal (`return H { f: |x| x+k }` / `return (clo, 1)` / `return [clo]`, via aggregate-literal recursion in tail_escapes_capturing_closure). Both walkers are non-exhaustive on purpose — a missed container only UNDER-collects, never falsely rejects (full codegen 1746/0). STAYS OPEN: the feature itself (actually returning a capturing closure) is unimplemented, and ONE narrower silent-miscompile residual remains — a capturing closure stored into a LOCAL struct/Vec that is then returned via an identifier (`let h = H{f:|x|x+k}; return h`), which needs container-escape tracking (the escape-analysis slice). Severity stays high until that residual is guarded or the heap-env feature lands. A sound guard needs an EXHAUSTIVE 'f only ever a call callee' walker (refs_in_expr is unusable — lossy `_ => {}`, 33/~40 ExprKinds, a missed kind = a missed escape = UAF); cleaner end-state is inc-on-copy RC (fold in the shared-ownership slice) so nothing needs rejecting.
