Tests: escaping_capturing_closure_{container_push, container_insert, index_store, field_store}_is_rejected, store_escape_guard_does_not_over_reject. SLICE 1 LANDED — HEAP-ENV FEATURE + SOUND MISUSE GUARD 2026-06-23 (88bfa7de): the clo-rc1 WIP (bcf8472c, 'DO NOT MERGE — unsound') is now SOUND and merged. A function RETURNING a capturing closure (its direct closure-literal tail) gets a reference-counted HEAP env (emit_rc_alloc `{i64 refcount, env}`; body GEPs past the refcount); the owning `let f = make(..)` binding frees it via CleanupAction::FreeClosureEnv (RC-dec, free-at-0) at scope exit; POD captures only; the Slice-0 guard is relaxed for exactly that tail shape (func_tail_heap_closure_span). The missing ~80% — the misuse guard — is the new piece: reject_heap_env_misuse makes the feature SOUND by turning every not-yet-supported use of a heap-env binding into an honest E_ESCAPING_CLOSURE_NOT_YET instead of a UAF / double-free / leak. SUPPORTED: calling the binding in its owning function (`let f = make(21); f(21)` -> 42; multi-call `f(1); f(2)` -> freed once). REJECTED: return f, copy (`let g = f`), store (struct/tuple/array/Vec/index/field), pass-as-arg, capture-in-nested-closure, and an UNBOUND / mid-expr make() (`make();`, `make()(x)`, `return make()`, `[make()]`). The walk (expr_has_heap_env_misuse/block_has_heap_env_misuse) is EXHAUSTIVE over ExprKind/StmtKind with NO silent wildcard (a miss = a missed escape = UAF, so the compiler enforces coverage); `f(args)` recurses only the args (callee is the one sanctioned occurrence); inert unless some fn returns a heap-env closure. Verified: all of {return, copy, unbound, pass-arg, store-*, method-recv, if/match-arm, immediate-call} reject; RC env freed exactly once — Linux ASAN+LSan clean (asan_heap_env_closure_freed_no_leak, asan_heap_env_closure_multi_call_freed_no_leak). codegen 1771/0, par_codegen 123/0, memory_sanitizer 350/0. STAYS OPEN / HIGH: only the direct-tail return shape is implemented; OTHER shapes stay rejected-or-residual — an identifier-tail return (`let f = clo; f`) and aggregate returns are still guarded (not heap-env'd), and the STORE-escape residuals from the guard slices (a closure pushed into a call-init collection `let v = fresh(); v.push(clo); return v`, nested-in-branch stores) remain SILENT. The complete epic = heap-env for those remaining shapes + shared-ownership (inc-on-copy RC) so copy/store/return-again work rather than reject. SHARED-OWNERSHIP INC-ON-COPY — COPY SLICE LANDED 2026-06-28 (ca644379): the first shared-ownership slice — COPYING a heap-env binding (`let g = f`) — now WORKS rather than being rejected. A copy increments the shared RC env box's refcount (emit_heap_closure_env_inc, null-guarded, mirrors the FreeClosureEnv cleanup's box/refcount access inverted to +1 with no free) and registers g's OWN FreeClosureEnv cleanup; both owners RC-drop at scope exit so the one box is freed EXACTLY once. Marking g in heap_env_closure_vars makes copy-of-copy chains (`let g = f; let h = g`) transitively all heap-env bindings (each copy increments the same box). The misuse guard (reject_heap_env_misuse) is relaxed accordingly: pass-1 now collects copy bindings in a FORWARD scan (transitive), pass-2 sanctions a single-name `let g = f` copy RHS; everything else (return-again, store, pass-arg, capture-in-nested-closure, unbound make()) STAYS rejected by the same exhaustive no-wildcard walk. The codegen copy handler sits AHEAD of the generic fn-value let path (which would copy the fat pointer WITHOUT the inc -> under-count -> premature free / use-after-free). Verified: heap_env_binding_copied_runs (`let g = f`, both callable -> 43), heap_env_binding_copy_chain_runs (`let g = f; let h = g` -> 36); RC env freed exactly once — macOS ASAN clean + Linux LSan clean (asan_heap_env_closure_copy_freed_no_leak). codegen 1773/0, par_codegen 123/0, memory_sanitizer 351/0. STAYS OPEN / HIGH: return-again (`return f`) and store-in-aggregate still rejected (need the move-out-on-return ownership transfer + the aggregate-embedded closure-drop slices), and the earlier store-escape residuals (a closure pushed into a call-init collection `let v = fresh(); v.push(clo); return v`, nested-in-branch stores) remain SILENT. Next copy-class follow-on: reassignment `g = f` (drop-old + acquire-new). RETURN-AGAIN SLICE LANDED 2026-06-28 (5141672e): a heap-env closure binding may now be RE-RETURNED — `let f = make(k); return f;` (explicit top-level return) and `let f = make(k); f` (bare-identifier tail) — including a relay-of-a-relay and a copy-then-return. Was rejected by the misuse guard; now works. Model is MOVE-OUT (not inc-on-return), mirroring the existing Vec/String/Map/channel/SoA tail-return suppression: new neutralize_moved_closure_env_slot runtime-nulls the source fat pointer's env-pointer slot AFTER the return value is loaded, so the source's scope-exit FreeClosureEnv (null-guarded) no-ops and the live env box flows to the caller at the SAME refcount; the caller's `let r = relay(..)` already gets a FreeClosureEnv (relay is now in fns_returning_heap_env), so the box is freed EXACTLY once at the final owner. Runtime-null (not compile-time queue removal) is branch-safe by construction. Wired at BOTH return paths: the tail-return hub (suppress_cleanup_for_tail_return, call_dispatch.rs) and the explicit-return arm (exprs.rs), which are mutually exclusive per exit path. Detection: compute_fns_returning_heap_env is now a FIXPOINT — seeded by direct capturing-closure-literal tails (func_tail_heap_closure_span), then iterated to add any fn whose top-level tail OR top-level `return` is a bare heap-env binding (func_returns_heap_env_binding; bindings collected by the same forward scan as the guard, transitive through copies) until stable, so a relay-of-a-relay is recognized once its inner relay is. is_heap_env_producing_call refactored to is_heap_env_producing_call_in(set) so the fixpoint can query the partially-built set. Guard (reject_heap_env_misuse) relaxed in lockstep: a bare heap-env-binding TAIL and a top-level `return <bare binding>;` are sanctioned; the EXHAUSTIVE no-wildcard walk is unchanged. Verified: heap_env_binding_returned_again_runs / _tail_runs / relay_of_relay_runs / copy_then_return_runs all -> 42, branch_buried_return_is_rejected stays an honest error; RC env freed exactly once across all four shapes — macOS ASAN clean + Linux LSan clean (asan_heap_env_closure_returned_again_freed_no_leak). codegen 1777/0, par_codegen 123/0, memory_sanitizer 352/0. STAYS OPEN / HIGH: store-in-aggregate (struct/tuple/array/Vec) and pass-as-arg still rejected (need aggregate-embedded closure drop + borrow-vs-own param classification), a BRANCH-BURIED return and a direct `return make(..)` / tail `make(..)` (unbound call-tail) stay rejected (sound under-approximations), and the earlier store-escape residuals (closure pushed into a call-init collection, nested-in-branch stores) remain SILENT. Remaining epic = store-in-aggregate (with embedded drop) + reassignment `g = f`. STORE-IN-STRUCT SLICE LANDED 2026-06-28 (e556fd01): a FRESH heap-env closure may now be STORED into a struct literal field — `let h = H { f: make(k) }` — and the struct field-CALLED (`(h.f)(x)`) and its non-closure fields read; was rejected. The env box in the field is RC-dropped per-INSTANCE: codegen registers a FreeClosureEnv on the struct field's GEP (register_struct_literal_heap_env_field_drops, called from the let-binding struct-tracking block; the Fn field is an inline {fn_ptr, env_ptr} fat pointer so the GEP is exactly the fat_alloca the cleanup expects; fresh make() leaves rc=1 so the field drop frees it once at h's scope exit). CRUCIAL soundness point: this is INSTANCE-specific, NOT the type-driven __karac_drop_struct_<S> — the SAME struct type may elsewhere hold a same-frame STACK-env closure (`H { f: |x| x+base }`) whose env is a stack alloca, and a type-level RC-dec would free() a stack address / corrupt the captured value. The misuse guard gained an AGGREGATE-OWNER class (heap_env_aggregate_owners: struct local -> its heap-env-call field names, built in pass-1; reject_heap_env_misuse is now &mut self and stashes it for the exhaustive walk): the construction `let h = H {..}` is sanctioned (only the heap-env-call fields; other fields still walked), the Call arm sanctions `(h.f)(x)`, the FieldAccess arm allows a non-closure field read (`h.n`) but flags a non-call projection of a closure field (`return h.f` / `let g = h.f`), and the Identifier arm flags a bare `h` (any escape). REJECTED (sound): returning the owning struct (`return h` — its field drop would free the env the caller holds; the aggregate-RETURN feature is a later slice), projecting the closure field out (`let g = h.f`), passing h as an arg, and a BINDING source (`H { f: f }` — needs inc-on-store co-ownership, the next store sub-slice). Verified: heap_env_stored_in_struct_field_runs / _with_data_field_runs -> 42, and {struct_returned, field_projection, binding_stored, struct_passed_as_arg} all rejected; field env freed exactly once — macOS ASAN clean + Linux LSan clean (asan_heap_env_stored_in_struct_field_freed_no_leak). codegen 1783/0, par_codegen 123/0, memory_sanitizer 353/0. STAYS OPEN / HIGH: tuple/array/Vec field stores and the binding-source struct store still rejected; the owning struct still can't ESCAPE (return/copy/store/arg) — that needs aggregate move-out + a caller-side aggregate field-drop (analogous to fns_returning_heap_env but struct-typed); and the earlier store-escape residuals (closure pushed into a call-init collection, nested-in-branch stores) remain SILENT. Remaining epic = binding-source + tuple/array/Vec stores, aggregate escape, and reassignment `g = f`. BINDING-SOURCE STORE SUB-SLICE LANDED 2026-06-28 (e516bad5): a heap-env closure BINDING may now be STORED into a struct literal field — `let h = H { f: f }` (and through a copy, `let g = f; H { f: g }`) — where previously only a FRESH call source (`H { f: make(k) }`) was allowed. Closures are COPY-semantics in Kara (proven by the slice-1 `let g = f; f(1); g(2)` test), so the source binding `f` STAYS USABLE after the store and the struct field CO-OWNS the env: codegen bumps the shared RC env's refcount at the store (register_struct_literal_heap_env_field_drops now loads the field's inline {fn_ptr,env_ptr} fat and calls emit_heap_closure_env_inc for an Identifier-in-heap_env_closure_vars field, mirroring the `let g = f` inc-on-copy; a fresh-call field is still rc=1 with NO inc), so BOTH the source binding's scope-exit FreeClosureEnv AND the field's per-instance FreeClosureEnv fire and the box is freed EXACTLY once. The misuse guard grew to match: struct_literal_heap_env_call_fields -> struct_literal_heap_env_store_fields(binds) collects a binding-source field (Identifier in binds) as an aggregate-owner field too, and the construction-walk skips those binding fields (else the bare `f` in `H { f: f }` would be flagged as an escaping binding). COMPOSITE soundness verified: store a binding then MOVE the source out via a tail return — the store inc's to rc 2, the move-out neutralizes the source's drop and hands the box to the caller, the owner struct's field drop decs to 1 at the relay's scope exit, and the caller's binding frees the last ref (freed once across the move boundary). STILL REJECTED (sound): the owning struct can't ESCAPE even with a binding-source field (return/copy/store/pass `h` — heap_env_binding_owner_struct_returned_is_rejected), and projecting the closure field out (`let g = h.f`) / passing `h` as an arg stay rejected. Verified: heap_env_binding_stored_in_struct_field_runs / _copy_stored_in_struct_with_data_field_runs / _stored_then_source_returned_runs -> 42, _binding_owner_struct_returned_is_rejected; field env freed exactly once across all three owners — macOS ASAN clean + Linux LSan clean (asan_heap_env_binding_stored_in_struct_field_freed_no_leak -> 83). codegen 1786/0, par_codegen 123/0, memory_sanitizer 354/0. STAYS OPEN / HIGH: tuple/array/Vec field stores still rejected; the owning struct still can't ESCAPE (return/copy/store/arg) — needs aggregate move-out + a caller-side aggregate field-drop (analogous to fns_returning_heap_env but struct-typed); reassignment `g = f` still rejected; and the earlier store-escape residuals (closure pushed into a call-init collection, nested-in-branch stores) remain SILENT. Remaining epic = tuple/array/Vec stores, aggregate escape, and reassignment. AGGREGATE-ESCAPE SUB-SLICE LANDED 2026-06-28 (39bfd196): a function may now RETURN a struct that OWNS a heap-env closure field — `fn build(k) -> H { let h = H { f: make(k) }; return h }` (explicit `return h` AND bare-tail `h`), with the caller `let r = build(k)` then field-calling `(r.f)(x)` and reading sibling non-closure fields. The env box MOVES OUT inside the struct at the SAME refcount: the callee neutralizes the owner's field env slot on the returning path (neutralize_moved_aggregate_env_slots runtime-nulls each owned field's inline {fn_ptr,env_ptr} env-pointer in h's alloca, so its scope-exit FreeClosureEnv no-ops; the already-materialized by-value return keeps the env), and the caller registers an instance FreeClosureEnv on each owned field of `r` (register_aggregate_call_heap_env_field_drops, NO inc — pure move-out) so `r`'s scope exit frees it exactly once. NEW detection pre-pass compute_fns_returning_heap_env_aggregate (a FIXPOINT, run after compute_fns_returning_heap_env) maps each fn -> the returned struct's owned-field NAMES; it shares owner collection with the misuse guard via the factored collect_heap_env_binds_and_owners (binds = closure bindings; owners = struct locals from a struct-literal store OR an aggregate-returning CALL result). The guard sanctions `return h`/tail `h` for an owner (mirroring the bare-binding return sanction) and `let r = build(k)` as an owner source while still walking the call's ARGS (so a heap-env binding passed as an arg to an aggregate builder is still rejected — the arg-escape hole). Codegen records per-owner (struct-type, field-index) in heap_env_owner_fields (reset per fn, iterated in DECLARED field order for deterministic IR) for the move-out. RELAY-of-aggregate (`fn relay(k) -> H { let r = build(k); return r }`) works via the fixpoint. STILL REJECTED (sound): COPYING an owner (`let s = r`), reassigning a field (`r.f = g`), passing the owner as an arg (`use_h(h)`), and projecting the closure field out (`let g = h.f`). Verified: heap_env_struct_returned_runs / _tail_runs / _with_data_field_runs / _aggregate_relay_runs / _binding_owner_struct_returned_runs -> 42, plus _struct_passed_as_arg_is_rejected and _binding_passed_to_aggregate_builder_is_rejected; each env freed exactly once across the move boundary — macOS ASAN clean + Linux LSan clean (asan_heap_env_aggregate_returned_freed_no_leak -> 124). codegen 1794/0, par_codegen 123/0, memory_sanitizer 356/0. STAYS OPEN / HIGH: tuple/array/Vec field stores still rejected; owner COPY (`let s = r`) and field REASSIGNMENT (`r.f = g`, `g = f`) still rejected (need aggregate co-ownership / drop-old); passing an owner as a by-value ARG still rejected (needs callee-borrows-or-owns analysis); and the earlier store-escape residuals (closure pushed into a call-init collection, nested-in-branch stores/returns) remain SILENT-rejected. Remaining epic = tuple/array/Vec stores, owner copy + arg-pass, and reassignment. TUPLE-STORE SUB-SLICE LANDED 2026-06-28 (7888a761): a heap-env closure may now be STORED into a TUPLE element — `let t = (make(k), n)` (FRESH call) and `let t = (f, n)` (heap-env BINDING source) — then tuple-index-CALLED `(t.0)(x)` with non-closure elements (`t.1`) read. A tuple is a by-value aggregate `{ e0, e1, .. }`, so a `Fn` element is an inline {fn_ptr,env_ptr} fat pointer: codegen registers an instance FreeClosureEnv on each heap-env element's GEP (register_tuple_literal_heap_env_elem_drops, called from the let tuple-tracking block, ahead of the type-driven tuple drop which leaves Fn elements alone). A fresh-call element is rc=1 (no inc); a binding-source element COPIES the source fat so it co-owns the box — the refcount is bumped (emit_heap_closure_env_inc), and both the source binding's drop and the element drop fire → freed exactly once. The misuse guard gained a TUPLE-OWNER class (heap_env_tuple_owners: tuple local -> heap-env element INDEX set, built in pass 1 alongside the struct aggregate owners; reset per fn): construction `let t = (..)` is sanctioned (only the heap-env elements; others walked), the Call arm sanctions `(t.0)(x)` (TupleIndex callee on a tuple owner), the TupleIndex arm rejects a non-call projection of a closure element (`let g = t.0`) but allows a non-closure element read (`t.1`), and the Identifier arm rejects a bare `t` (any escape). STILL REJECTED (sound): the owning tuple can't ESCAPE — `return t` / tail `t` (tuple escape, like the earlier struct store-only slice before aggregate-escape) and projecting the element out. Verified: heap_env_stored_in_tuple_runs / _binding_stored_in_tuple_runs / _two_closures_in_tuple_runs -> 42, _tuple_returned_is_rejected, _tuple_elem_projection_is_rejected; each env freed exactly once — macOS ASAN clean + Linux LSan clean (asan_heap_env_stored_in_tuple_freed_no_leak -> 72). Also fixed a PRE-EXISTING `doc_lazy_continuation` clippy lint in src/codegen/column.rs (a `+ bool` wrapped doc line read as a markdown bullet) that CI's no-llvm clippy job never compiled — landed as a standalone chore commit. codegen 1802/0, par_codegen 123/0, memory_sanitizer 359/0. ARRAY-STORE SLICE LANDED (f7b9851c): a heap-env closure may be STORED in a FIXED-SIZE array element (`let a: Array[Fn,N] = [make(k), ..]` fresh-call, or `[f, ..]` heap-env binding source) and called back through the array index `(a[i])(x)` (constant OR dynamic index). Each element env is RC-dropped per-INSTANCE via a FreeClosureEnv on the array element GEP (build_gep [0, idx]) — separate from any type-driven array drop (a {ptr,ptr} Fn element reads as POD, so without this the env would leak); a fresh element stays rc 1, a binding source bumps the env refcount (co-ownership, source stays usable, freed once). The array twin of the tuple-store registrar; only the GEP form differs (array build_gep [0,idx] vs tuple build_struct_gep). The misuse guard gained an ARRAY-OWNER class (heap_env_array_owners: array local -> heap-env element INDEX set, built in reject_heap_env_misuse, reset per fn; only an ExprKind::ArrayLiteral RHS qualifies — a bare [..] lowers to a Vec PrefixCollectionLiteral, the deferred dynamic-length slice, so the Vec form stays rejected): construction sanctioned (only heap-env elements; others walked), the Call arm sanctions `(a[i])(x)` (Index callee on an array owner), the Index arm rejects a non-call projection of a closure element (`let g = a[i]`; constant index keyed on membership, dynamic index conservatively rejected), the Identifier arm rejects a bare `a` (any escape). Arrays are homogeneous, so an array-of-closures has no non-closure sibling read (unlike a tuple). STILL REJECTED (sound): the owning array can't ESCAPE (`return a` / tail `a`) and a closure element can't be projected out — only call-through. STAYS OPEN / HIGH: Vec (`v.push(make(k))` / `Vec[make(k)]`) element stores still rejected — the hard one, needs a dynamic per-element drop loop at Vec teardown (unknown length); tuple/array/Vec ESCAPE not supported; owner COPY (`let s = t` / `let s = r` / `let s = a`) and field/element REASSIGNMENT still rejected; by-value owner ARG-pass still rejected. Remaining epic = Vec stores, container escape, owner copy + arg-pass, and reassignment. VEC-STORE SLICE LANDED (c11f3492), the first DYNAMIC-count drop in the epic: a heap-env closure may be PUSHED into a `Vec[Fn]` (`let v: Vec[Fn] = Vec.new()`/`Vec.with_capacity(..)`; `v.push(make(k))` fresh or `v.push(f)` for a heap-env binding) and called back via `(v[i])(x)` (const OR dynamic index), `v.len()` etc. Each live element's env is RC-dropped by a DYNAMIC `0..len` drop LOOP at the Vec's scope exit — the dynamic-length analog of the array/tuple per-slot drops — reusing the existing `elem_agg_drop` drain (track_vec_of_aggs_var) with a synthesized one-per-module `__karac_vec_elem_closure_env_drop` fn (the FreeClosureEnv logic hoisted to take an element ptr). A fresh push leaves the element rc 1; a binding push bumps the env refcount (co-ownership, source stays usable, freed once). The misuse guard gained a VEC-OWNER class (heap_env_vec_owners: a fresh-ctor `Vec[Fn]` binding that receives >=1 heap-env push, detected recursively incl. loops/branches; reset per fn): it sanctions `v.push(<heap-env>)`, `(v[i])(x)`, and read-only len/is_empty/capacity, and REJECTS escape (`return v`), projection (`let g = v[i]`), moving/aliasing methods (pop/remove/...), and a non-heap-env push — a mixed heap-env+stack-env Vec can't be drop-classified at runtime, so it is rejected, never miscompiled (the unconditional loop can't free a stack address). AUTO-PAR FIX (same epic): a heap-env closure's fat pointer + RC env does NOT survive the auto-par par-group return-struct join (env pointer mis-transferred), so compute_return_slots_checked now bails any group that CONSTRUCTS a heap-env closure, or whose return slot is a closure value (the latter gated to programs that define an escaping closure, leaving closure-free code untouched), to sequential codegen — mirrors the existing destructure-bind / captured-mutation bail-outs. Surfaced because `let f = make(k)` got grouped with an independent `let v = Vec.new()` under the DEFAULT auto-par build, making `v.push(f)` read garbage; A/B verified across default auto-par, KARAC_AUTO_PAR=0, and the interpreter oracle. CONTAINER-ESCAPE SLICE LANDED (40e682eb), the by-value half: a fn may now RETURN a TUPLE or fixed-size ARRAY owning heap-env closure elements (bare tail or top-level `return t`), and the caller's `let r = build(..)` binding adopts the env boxes. VEC-ESCAPE SLICE LANDED (e6856fba), completing container escape: a fn may now RETURN a closure-owning `Vec[Fn]` (bare tail / `return v`), and the caller's `let r = build(..)` binding adopts the dynamic per-element drop loop. Strikingly, this needed NO new codegen — only detection + guard — because the existing Vec move-out + Vec-store registration already compose: the callee's tail-return cap-zero (suppress_source_vec_cleanup_for_arg) makes its FreeVecBuffer `cap>0` guard skip the WHOLE drop incl. the closure loop (buffer moved out by value), and the caller's `let r = build()` is recognized as a Vec OWNER, so the existing Vec-store registration (vec_elem_types[r] populated by inference) registers the `0..len` __karac_vec_elem_closure_env_drop loop on r — verified in @main IR. SLICE container owner by-value ARG-PASS (TUPLE / array / Vec) LANDED (4462c50a): extends the struct owner arg-pass borrow to a heap-env TUPLE / array / `Vec[Fn]` OWNER passed BY VALUE to a borrows-only callee — one that only CALLS its closure element(s) via `(t.0)(x)` / `(a[i])(x)` / `(v[i])(x)` and never returns / projects / stores / re-binds it. CRUCIALLY this holds for `Vec[Fn]` too: by-value arg-pass passes the Vec header by value and does NOT zero the caller's cap (unlike `let w = v`, a MOVE), so it is a borrow, not a move — confirmed empirically by ASAN (no double-free / UAF) + owner-reuse-after-call. SLICE closure BINDING REASSIGNMENT LANDED (30986b39) — the first REASSIGNMENT form and the first NON-guard-only piece of the epic. Reassigning a heap-env closure BINDING is now supported: `g = make(j)` (fresh env, a MOVE) and `g = f` (binding source, the SHARED env, a COPY) where `g` is a heap-env closure binding. CODEGEN (stmts.rs Assign / Identifier-target arm) follows the RC setter rule (retain new -> store -> release old): save `g`'s CURRENT fat pointer, inc the new env when the RHS is a binding copy (a fresh `make(j)` already carries its +1), store the new fat, then RC-drop the saved old env via a new shared `emit_heap_closure_env_dec` helper (factored out of the scope-exit FreeClosureEnv cleanup, which now loads + calls it). So `g`'s old env is freed exactly once at the reassignment, the new env exactly once at scope exit, and on a copy the source `f` stays a live co-owner (its own scope-exit drop balances the inc). POSITION-AGNOSTIC: the hook keys only off the target name being in heap_env_closure_vars, so it works at the top level, nested in a branch, in a LOOP (the drop-old fires once per execution -> every intermediate env freed once), and composes with the return-of-binding escape (`g = make(b); g`). Reassigning an ELEMENT of a heap-env `Vec[Fn]` owner is now supported: `v[i] = make(j)` (fresh env, a MOVE) and `v[i] = g` (binding source, the SHARED env, a COPY). Every heap-env closure place is now supported: RETURN (bare tail / top-level return, branch-leaf), STORE (struct field / tuple / array / Vec element), COPY/MOVE (struct/tuple/array owner COPY, Vec owner MOVE, binding copy), ESCAPE (aggregate / container move-out + caller adopt), by-value ARG-PASS BORROW (binding + struct/tuple/array/Vec owner to a borrows-only callee), and REASSIGNMENT (binding g=f/g=make, struct field r.f=.., Vec element v[i]=..). The original soundness hole — an escaping capturing closure reading a freed stack env — is fully resolved: escaping closures get an RC heap env box, every owner/use site is RC-accounted (inc on copy, dec/free at scope exit, move-out neutralize + caller adopt on escape, drop-old on reassign), and the misuse guard over-rejects (never miscompiles) any not-yet-modeled shape. ===== | be2ef68e |
| B-2026-06-22-3 | cli | low | `--bindings component` (the wasm_wasi default) emitted NON-reproducible component bytes — three builds of identical source produced three DIFFERENT SHA256 at the SAME byte length; `--bindings none` (core module) was always byte-identical. NOT HashMap/iteration-order (the initial hypothesis): a `cmp -l` of two captured cores showed exactly 2 differing bytes, both inside the `name` custom section — `...\x04name\x00! karac_9013_filter_core.core.wasm` vs `...9066...`; `wasm-tools component new` is itself deterministic on fixed input, and the embedded-WIT text is already deterministic (collect_host_fns/collect_wasm_exports iterate `program.items` in source order). Root cause: the embedded-component build links the C-ABI core module to a process-unique SCRATCH file named `karac_<pid>_<stem>.core.wasm` (single-file, src/cli.rs) / `karac_proj_<pid>_<pkg>.core.wasm` (project), and wasm-ld bakes that basename verbatim into the module-name subsection of the wasm `name` section; `wasm-tools component embed`/`component new` then carry it into the final component. Two builds = two processes = two pids → the component differed in exactly the pid digits (same length whenever the pids share a digit width, different bytes always). `--bindings none` was immune because it links straight to the stable `<stem>.wasm` output path (no pid). FIXED by linking the core module under a source-DERIVED basename (`<stem>.core.wasm`) inside a process-unique DIRECTORY — new `componentize::link_core_scratch(stem)` reuses `scratch_dir()` (pid+counter) for the enclosing dir, so parallel builds stay collision-free on disk while the embedded module name — and thus the whole component — is byte-identical run to run; both link sites (single-file + project) and their cleanup (remove the scratch dir, not just the file) updated. Side benefit: the shipped artifact no longer leaks an internal temp path into its name section. Regression: tests/cli.rs `wasm_wasi_component_is_byte_reproducible` builds the same source twice in two distinct processes and asserts byte-identical components (an export drives the WIT embed leg too); a manual 3x build now yields a single SHA. Surfaced via the bench/wasm_size size receipt (the Kāra component brotli figure jittered ~0.2% run-to-run). | — |
| B-2026-06-22-4 | codegen | high | Calling a closure stored in a struct field silently returns 0 under `karac build` — `(h.f)(arg)` miscompiles (codegen-only; `karac run` is CORRECT). A closure value (the {fn_ptr, env_ptr} fat pointer) stored in a struct field and invoked through a parenthesized field-access callee — `struct H { f: Fn(i64)->i64 }  let h = H { f: |x| x * 2 };  (h.f)(21)` — typechecks and `karac build` links+runs, but the call evaluates to 0 instead of invoking the closure. Reproduced SAME-FRAME and NON-CAPTURING, so it is independent of the B-2026-06-22-2 escaping-stack-env hole — a distinct closure-call-DISPATCH gap. Confirmed divergence: the same program under `karac run` (tree-walk interpreter) prints the correct 42; only the LLVM backend returns 0. Root-cause hypothesis: compile_closure_call (src/codegen/closures.rs ~L1057) lowers an indirect closure call ONLY when the callee is a NAMED identifier present in closure_fn_types (`match self.closure_fn_types.get(name) { Some(t) => .., None => return Ok(i64 const 0) }`); a FieldAccess callee (and presumably index / tuple-index / call-result place-expressions yielding a closure value) never reaches the fat-pointer extract+indirect-call path, so it falls through to the None const-0 stub. Notably NO existing codegen test RUNS a closure call through a struct field — the only `(x.f)(..)` snippets in tests/codegen.rs are expect_err escape-rejection tests that never execute the program, so the gap was invisible. FIX: generalize closure-call lowering to accept a closure VALUE produced by any expression (field access, index, tuple-index, parenthesized expr, call result) — evaluate it to the {fn_ptr, env_ptr} fat pointer and emit the env-first indirect call — and add E2E tests that actually RUN `(h.f)(arg)` and a Vec[Fn]-index call, asserting parity with `karac run`. Two Value variants — `TaskGroup` (stateless marker — the group carries no live task state because children run eagerly) and `TaskHandle(Box<Value>)` (carries the child's already-computed result), each with Display + variant_name arms; a `TaskGroup.new` associated-call arm (sibling of `Atomic.new`) returns the marker; a `spawn` builtin-identifier arm + shared `eval_spawn_closure` run the closure eagerly at the spawn site and box the result into a `TaskHandle` (a panicking child dominates via pending_cf — fail-fast parity with par {} / collect_all); receiver-typed method dispatch routes `TaskGroup.spawn` (run child, return handle), `TaskGroup.cancel` (no-op — children already ran), and `TaskHandle.join` (deliver the boxed result), gated on the concrete receiver value so they never shadow `Command.spawn` / `String.join`. The join-at-spawn model is observably identical to the parallel codegen for the order-independent fan-out/join shape the `ScopeLocal` rules permit (a handle cannot escape its spawning scope, so cross-task communication is confined to shared Atomic/Mutex cells whose interpreter models are already thread-safe); it deliberately does NOT model programs that observe shared mutable state BETWEEN spawn and the group's drop barrier (those read a racy, unsynchronized value under codegen too). ROOT CAUSE (git-bisected to f6d9873f, the phase-12 #34 stdlib-collision fix): `register_baked_stdlib` (src/typechecker/env_build.rs) implemented the collision-skip at MODULE granularity — when the user program redefined any struct/enum a baked module exports, the ENTIRE module was dropped from env injection. #34's target (the self-host `struct Parser` vs std.cli's `Parser`, so `Parser.new(tokens)` resolves to the user impl) was met, but the hammer was far too wide: redefining a single common type name (`Response`) also dropped its sibling exports (`Server`, `Request`, `HttpError`, `impl Server`, `impl Request`), so `Server.serve` no longer resolved via the `env.impls` associated-fn lookup in expr_ops.rs. FIX: make the collision-skip per-ITEM instead of per-module — drop only the redefined `struct`/`enum` and any impl block whose target type is that name; keep all sibling types, their impls, and free functions always-injected. This still satisfies #34 (the user's `struct Parser` + `impl Parser` become the sole `Parser` surface — std.cli's `struct Parser` AND `impl Parser` are both dropped, so `Parser.new` binds to the user impl, which is exactly why dropping the type WITHOUT its impls was unsafe and the per-item filter drops both) without amputating the rest of the module. A kept sibling impl whose signature names the redefined type now references the USER's type through the shared env — identical to the pre-f6d9873f shadowing behavior, and only sites that actually call such a sibling are affected (those were already the user's to reconcile). NOT one of the two same-day suspects (489825fa codegen / 12c2346f atomic) that predated the report — both are codegen/atomic-only and structurally cannot emit a typecheck NoMethodFound; the bisect over c119c1f6..d280af49 (1074 commits) pinned the real culprit at f6d9873f (2026-06-18). The `compiling_stdlib` gate (a stdlib module self-compiling must not skip itself) is unchanged. ROOT CAUSE: the interpreter's pattern matcher (pattern_match.rs `PatternKind::Binding`) classifies a bare PascalCase identifier as a unit-variant pattern only when `self.env.get(name)` returns a unit `EnumVariant` value — the mechanism user-enum unit variants rely on — otherwise it is a catch-all binding that matches anything. `register_items` (interpreter.rs) registered the built-in `Ordering` (and `MemoryOrdering`) variants under their QUALIFIED names only (`"Ordering.Less"`), so `env.get("Less")` was None and bare `Less` fell through to the always-true binding, making the first arm win. | B-2026-07-01-10 | other | med | Stats.* arguments MOVE the slice: `let v: Vec[f64] = ...; Stats.sum(v); Stats.mean(v)` is rejected by the ownership checker ('value v moved here, used again here') even though the runtime semantics never consume the argument (the codegen module doc explicitly documents 'the slice is a borrow' and only frees fresh-temp args). Root cause: Kara declares parameter modes on the callee (`ref` = borrow, bare = move; call sites never write `ref`), and runtime/stdlib/stats.kara declares `xs: Slice[f64]` WITHOUT `ref` — so every Stats call consumes its vec under `karac check`/`build`, making two statistics over one dataset impossible without cloning. The whole codegen test suite masks this because the run_program harness never gates on ownership errors (tests/codegen.rs run_program_capturing_inner computes ownershipcheck only to feed codegen's RC-fallback surface — test_e2e_stats_empty_slice passes v FOUR times and stays green while `karac check` rejects the same program). NOT Stats-specific in mechanism (any bare Slice/Vec param moves — that part is the language design), but the stdlib signature contradicts both the documented borrow semantics and obvious usage. FIX DIRECTION: declare the stats.kara params `ref` (audit interpreter/codegen arg handling + the fresh-temp free gate first: a `ref` param changes the ownership pass's view, and materialize_owned_temp on a fresh literal arg must still fire), or give `Slice[T]` params borrow mode by default as the type's design intent; and consider making the codegen harness surface ownership errors so the suite stops masking this class. FIXED 1fd799b7: all 13 stats.kara params declared `ref Slice[f64]`, AND the root enabler — collect_callee_param_modes/collect_method_param_modes walked only the USER program's items, so NO baked-stdlib signature's declared mode ever reached the ownership pass's call-arg classification (the whole baked surface was consume-default); both collectors now walk STDLIB_PROGRAMS first with user entries overriding. Probed: 13-fn reuse over one dataset, borrow-mutate-borrow, fresh temp args (freed via ref-rvalue materialization), i64 elements — check-clean, interp/codegen matched, zero leaks. The harness-masking half (run_program harness never gates on ownership errors, so the codegen suite stayed green on programs karac check rejects) remains a test-infra follow-up — not fixed here. | 1fd799b7 |

| B-2026-07-01-12 | codegen | med | Map.get payload MOVED OUT of the borrow-bound match arm double-frees against the map's stored value — `let s = match m.get(k) { Some(x) => x, None => f"none" }; println(s)` on a plain Map[i64, String] exits 133 TODAY (probe p9_string_moveout.ka 2026-07-01; interpreter prints fine — value semantics copy). | B-2026-07-03-2 | codegen | med | A method declared `-> Self` was broken end-to-end under `karac build` for EVERY form (inherent method, trait impl, static constructor); `karac run` masked it by executing past the typecheck warning, and selfhost/examples never exercise `-> Self` under build (0 occurrences), so the gap was latent. Three legs: (1) TYPECHECK — a `Self` return-type annotation lowers to `Named{"Self"}` (or `TypeParam("Self")` when "Self" is an in-scope generic), and the body's concrete tail type is not assignable to it, so `check_function` rejected valid code with "expected 'Self', found 'W'". (2) CODEGEN PROTOTYPE — `llvm_return_type` hit the unknown-name `i64` fall-through for `Self`, so a struct-returning `-> Self` fn's LLVM type mismatched its aggregate `ret` (module-verify hard failure). (3) CALL-SITE TYPING — the value-receiver method-call return type substituted only the impl's generics, leaving `Self` unresolved, so `a.m()` typed as `Self` and downstream field reads returned 0 (silent miscompile). FIXED (f6e35b1c): items.rs `resolve_self_in_type` resolves `Self` in the lowered return type to the concrete impl target inside `check_function` (identity for a trait default body); helpers.rs `rewrite_self_in_type_expr` rewrites `Self` in the synthesized impl-method's return type before prototype build; expr_method_call.rs resolves `Self` in the method-call return type + params to the concrete receiver.
